"O, children, since I have completed this book for you, which is the last of medical science, to achieve its completion and purpose, it seems to me that I should fulfill my promise to you with this treatise on surgery."
Because the art of surgery is greatly neglected in our region and time, and its science has greatly declined, leaving only a few traces behind. And unless it were for some brief descriptions found in the books of the Ancients, which are now muddled and unclear due to changes over time, leading to errors and misconceptions, so that their true meanings are obscured and their strength diminished.
"And it seems to me that I should revive this art with a well-ordered treatise following the path of explanation, declaration, and abbreviation; also including figures of cautery instruments and other tools used in surgery, both for addition to the explanation and preparation thereof, which is necessary."
"But the reason why there are few skilled surgeons in our time is because the art of medicine is lengthy, and its practitioner must first be well-exercised in the science of anatomy, which contains knowledge of the joints of members and their shapes, connections, and separations; also knowing the bones, nerves, and sinews, their number, size, and location of the pulsating veins and quiet ones, and the places where they discharge."
"And therefore Hippocrates said that 'in words little, but in deeds much, especially in surgery.'"
"But we have already said this at the beginning of this book: whoever is not knowledgeable about what we have said about anatomy will surely fall into error, causing many deaths among men, as I have seen too often. For some are formed in this science but lack its knowledge and experience."
"For I once saw a foolish and inexperienced doctor who incised an escrofulous abscess in the neck of a woman, cutting some arteries of the neck so that much blood flowed, causing the woman to suddenly die."
"And I saw another doctor who tried to remove a stone from the bladder of a man who had fallen into that state, and the stone was large. He came upon it and removed that stone with a piece of the bladder wall, causing that man to die on the third day."
"And I had already foreseen that this would happen, and when I saw the size of the stone and the condition of the patient, I knew for certain that he would die."
"And I saw another doctor who was paid by our Duke to practice surgery. He attended a blacksmith who had fractured his hip joint; due to the doctor's ignorance, he reduced the fracture with pillows and bandages of great tension, not allowing room for respiration."
"And he kept him bound up according to his desires, and then released him, and allowed him to rest for several days, commanding that the bandages be loosened. And so it happened that the hip joint became inflamed, and the thigh flesh putrefied, resulting in ruin."
"And I was called to him, and I prepared to loosen the bandages. And thus there was tranquility and alleviation of his pain."
"But nonetheless, corruption was already confirmed in the member, so that I could not prevent it. The corruption did not cease to spread throughout the limb until the patient perished."
"And I saw another doctor who perforated a cancerous abscess. It was soon ulcerated, and the evil of it greatly magnified in its lord."
"This is because the cancerous caul is pure of melancholic humor. Therefore, it should not be cauterized with iron in its entirety, but only where necessary on the member that suffers from it."
"And therefore, my children, it is necessary for you that the operation with the hand be divided into two parts: one is the operation associated with health, and the other is the work in which there is danger in the greatest situations."
"And I have already mentioned this throughout the entire book wherever operation is spoken of where there is danger and fear. Therefore, it is necessary for you to keep watch over this and leave that alone, so that foolish people may not find an opportunity to speak against you."
"And therefore take up your weapons with sincerity and protection of God, and deal with illnesses with gentleness and firmness."
"And use the best way by the grace of God to bring about health and praise-worthy success. Leave behind terrible illnesses that are difficult to cure, and put aside your weapons at that which makes you fearful, so that you may remain steadfast in your faith and in your name: for more remains to your glory, both now and in the future, than in your sanctity."
"Wherefore, as I have said in some of my writings:" "Do not treat illnesses badly, lest you be called bad doctors."
"And I have already divided this book into three parts."
"Here begins the division of the book, and first of the first part." "The first chapter ordered in this manner: regarding the weights of tools and their shapes, and concerning the instruments for burning, and that which is necessary in operation."
"Here begins the second part of the division:" "The second chapter: concerning incision and perforation, and of cupping glasses, compresses, and the extraction of arrows and similar things. This chapter is ordered regarding the shapes of instruments."
"The third chapter: concerning reduction and dislocation, and the cure of torticollis and similar conditions. This chapter is ordered regarding weights and the shapes of instruments."
"It is necessary for me to speak of the qualities of the cauteries used in that operation and their contraindications, and in what condition cautery should be prohibited."
"Therefore I say that the discussion of the qualities of cautery and its contraindications is lengthy and drawn-out, subtle in knowledge and secretive. Many wise men have spoken about it, and they disagree among themselves regarding this matter. It suffices for me to discuss a little of their sermons, fearing lengthiness."
"And therefore I say that cautery benefits universally every condition regarding matter or lacking matter, except for two conditions which are devoid of matter:"
"In the case of a dry and hot complexion that is disorderly; for some say that cautery is beneficial for this, but others say the opposite, that cautery is not suitable for an illness which is caused by heat and dryness, as fire's nature is heat and dryness, and it would be inappropriate for such an illness to be treated with something that is hot and dry."
"The one who says the opposite of this argues that cautery is beneficial in all dry and hot illnesses that occur in men's bodies. For when you compare the body of man and its humidity to the complexion of fire, you find that the body of man is cold."
"And I say, based on what that person has said, that I have experienced this many times in practice."
"However, it is not necessary to add anything more about this subject that has already been thoroughly discussed in the chapter on cautery through repeated exercises. For having understood the diversity of men's complexions and the disposition of illnesses in their members, as well as their causes, accidents, and duration, is sufficient."
"But in other complexions, there is no fear for you, and especially in hot and humid illnesses. For all doctors agree on these matters, and they are not divided regarding the benefit of cautery in those illnesses."
"And know, my children, that the secret of curing by cautery with fire and its goodness is spoken about in the chapter on cautery with medicine that burns. For fire is simple, whose action only reaches the member that is cauterized and does not harm any other adjacent member unless it causes some slight injury."
"But the action of burning medicine reaches those who have taken it in their members. Often it causes illness that is difficult to cure and often it harms."
"But fire, due to its sublimity and the goodness of its substance, does nothing but remove excesses. And this is already known to us through experience and long study in this art regarding the truth of causes; and for that reason I am excused from prolonging this discussion. However, if it were not hidden in my book in this passage about the secret of cautery with fire, and its operation on bodies and its expulsion by which illnesses are expelled, demonstrated philosophically, it would sharpen your minds."
"And know, my children, that they disagree about the time when cautery should be performed and they consider the best time to be in spring."
"And I say that cautery is convenient at all times because the harm caused by accidental time is submerged in the benefit of what is attracted by cautery. And especially if cautery is performed for pains or necessary surgeries, such as those that cannot wait due to fear of greater harm, which is worse than a small injury entering through time."
"And do not think that, children, this is only estimated by the vulgar people and foolish doctors. For they consider that in those illnesses which are cured by cautery, there is no recovery of time, and they leave it at that consequence."
"And the reason is not as they imagine it to be for this: that cautery is only in place of medicine which alters the complexion and dries out the humors which are the cause of pains."
"But nevertheless, cautery is preferable to medicine because of its volatility, virtue, and power of operation, and the greatness of its Lord."
"And it is possible that the illness returns at some time, according to the complexion of the sick person, the location of the illness, and the virtue of cautery, as well as what has been prepared in the body from the accumulation of excesses there, and what has been acquired through food and similar causes. But if cautery is administered for an subtle illness in a member with few excesses and humors, such as toothache or similar ones, it is possible that the pain does not return, but this happens rarely."
"And the common saying is that cautery is the last resort of medicine, and this saying is truer than they understand it to be. For they believe that nothing is cured by medicine or any other cause except cautery."
"And the cause is contrary to that; and the intention that cautery is the last resort of medicine only applies when other methods of treatment have been tried for certain illnesses and they have not worked. And then, at the end of the illness, cautery is administered, which is beneficial in this case." "And from now on, know that cautery is the last resort of medicine, not according to the intention understood by the vulgar and most foolish doctors."
"And the ancients said that cautery with gold is better than cautery with iron, and they did not say this except for the equality of gold and the sublimity of its substance."
"And they said that the location of cautery does not matter, which is not absolutely true. For I have seen and proven that this is not always the case, except in some bodies without others, and cautery with gold is good and better than with iron, as they said. But when you perform cautery with fire using gold, it is not clear to you because its ignition depends on the quantity of gold you desire according to its purity, and because it prepares itself to receive heat; if you apply ignition precisely on top of it, the gold will melt in the fire, and sometimes some plates fall into the fire due to the carelessness of the artisan."
"And for that reason, cautery should be performed with iron more lightly and more moderately according to the rectitude of its operation."
"And I have already arranged this chapter on cautery according to chapters and those of the head inside the weights, so that later you can ask me whatever you want about it."
Chapter one
"This cauterization addresses humidity and coldness, which are the accidental causes of such diseases as sodden flux, called corrosion, from the head to the parts of the eyes and ears flowing abundantly; also excessive sleeping, toothache, and throat pain, generally all illnesses caused by coldness, such as paralysis, epilepsy, apoplexy, and similar ones in those diseases."
"The form of this cauterization is as follows: first, you should command the sick person to evacuate the head with laxative medicine for three or four nights, depending on the virtue of the illness, the age and habit of the patient."
"And then command him to shave his head with a razor and also have him sit on a bench covered with wool or feathers, placing his feet on the ground."
"Then place the palm of your hand over the bridge of his nose between his eyebrows." "But first, when your middle finger reaches that spot, mark it with ink and then light the olive-oil cautery lamp, whose form is as follows:"
"And then place that on the marked spot in such a way that it descends gradually with your hand pressed down slightly while you rotate it."
"And then raise your hand lightly and observe the spot; if you see some of the bone already exposed on the head, about the size of a grain of barley, then lift your hand up again and replace it with another one until you see what I have told you to."
"Then take a pinch of salt and dissolve it on the site, leaving it there for three days."
"And then pause over the wound on the edge and leave it there until the skin of the fire is destroyed." "And then treat the area with a quadruple antibiotic ointment until healed."
"And as they said, when the plague is fully opened, the better it casts out the brace, because it is better and more beneficial."
"And some of them said that the spine should be cauterized down to the bone, and the cautery should be held there until any portion of the spinal cord is adhered."
"And then scrape off what adheres to the bone, and then it should be treated."
"And others said that with the cautery they should reach the end, so that it presses on the bone with great force until the bone breaks, and this is the form of alphecati minor:" "And they estimate from that place the fumes of the head expire."
"And let the wound remain open for a long time, and then treated until it is consolidated."
"But I do not see these two kinds of cautery in any whole person due to fear; and that, it seems to me, is better with health when they are; for the head is devitalized by the solution of continuity from such a wound as we have testified in other members, and more so when the head is naturally prone to disease."
"And the first kind of cautery is safer and better, in my opinion; and with that method and with that procedure there is health."
"Chapter II"
Of the Cautery of the Head
"When in the whole head there occurs chronic and long-lasting pain, and that is in prolonged disease, and they use plasters and poultices and fomentations and emplasters and ointments and cataplasms and similar things, and especially if it has already been cauterized with one cautery which did not profit from any of those causes, then consider whether the head of the patient is naturally strong in its creation; and if it is not weak or frail at all, then cauterize with another cautery a little lower than that one." "And then cauterize there over the horn of his head with a cautery until the cord is severed." "Cut the cord and uncover the bone the amount we have mentioned and cauterize there with a cautery at the last part of the head in the place which is called 'vess', — that is the place where cupping glasses are placed." "And be gentle in this, and do not uncover the bone, for by this method there is much less pain than with all other cauteries of the head."
"And I say this cautery in its place, for it is necessary that the cautery with which you cauterize the horns of the head and the occupit be more subtle than that with which you cauterize the middle part of the head; and this is its form."
"Chapter III"
"Of cauterization for non-ancient migraine."
"When, despite endeavoring to relieve the head of its sudden pain or if it is spread throughout the whole body, it has been evacuated with medicines for clearing the head and other appropriate treatment has been administered as indicated in the methods for illnesses; and yet no improvement occurs, then cauterization may be employed in one of two ways: either cauterization using an acutely burning medicine or by means of iron."
"To cauterize with a burning medicine, you should take some salt and pour it onto the affected area while scraping off both ends of it." "And appropriately, you should cut into the location of the pain in the temple with a sterile lance until blood flows from that precise spot, so that it may be concealed."
"And then strengthen it with pressure by applying constriction, leaving it there for the space of three hours. Then remove it and wipe off the salt, allowing the wound to dry for two or three days. Finally, apply a bandage over the submerged area until the location becomes better."
"And then treat it with an ointment so that it may heal."
"And if you wish to do this using some burning medicines which I have written about in the second treatise on burning medicines."
"Now, cauterization with iron according to this method is performed using a cautery that has this shape:"
"And it is called the 'closed nail' cautery, because its head is shaped like a nail with some curvature and a small prominence in the middle."
"And then place it on the location of the pain, hold your hand steady so that the heat of the cautery does not burn you, and slowly rotate the hot iron with moderate speed."
"And if the amount cauterized becomes equal to half of it due to the specificity of the blood vessels, then lift your hand away so that the artery is not cauterized any further, preventing bleeding."
"And then moisten the area with salt water and apply it to the location, leaving it there for three days. Then apply a poultice with a bandage, and treat it with an ointment until it heals."
"If you wish to cauterize the tip of the scalpel according to cautery, be careful not to cut an artery in this particular migraine that is not ancient."
Chapter Four
On cauterizing an ancient migraine.
When treating a migraine using the methods we have described for the previous cure and those listed in our divisions of illnesses, but finding that these treatments are ineffective, then it is necessary to cauterize with the scalpel cautery until it becomes red hot. Apply it to the location of the pain with a line of about half its length, or use the tip; then pause for a moment and strengthen the heat until you can hear the artery hiss and perceive the bone beneath.
However, it is necessary for you to be careful not to damage the continuity of the mandible, which is moved by mastication; not to burn the nerve or the muscles that move it; and not to cause spasms.
"And if it is about the safeguard and caution regarding bleeding from the artery that is opened, because there is fear during its opening, especially for those who are inexperienced, uninformed, and not skilled. Leave the operation until the beginning."
"And I will bring to mind the regulation of accidental bleeding from an artery according to its manner, in its proper place in this book."
"And if you see that this illness does not improve with this cautery and you see the patient's condition tolerable, then cauterize in the middle of the head as we have described, and treat the wound until it heals."
"And if you wish, administer the cautery that we mentioned in the chapter on ligature of an artery with cautery using two scalpels; this is a better and more certain cauterization."
Chapter Five
On cauterizing earaches.
When there is pain in the ear accompanied by fever and it has been treated with laxatives and other remedies mentioned in the division, but the pain persists, then heat the cautery called "puncta," which has this form:
Then apply the puncta to the ignition and move it around the entire ear like a wheel, or around each tympanic membrane if the pain is in one of them. Slowly move the cautery along the edge of the ear opening little by little, until you sense the location with its tip.
"And if you apply this cautery with ten punctures to the entire ear, and then treat those locations until they are healed."
Chapter Six
Burning of the throat.
The tumor that is treated and cured by cautery is not anything other than the species that come from a vein, as we have said in the division of diseases.
Avoid cautery of the species that occurs due to dryness or spasm of the nerve
When you treat that throat condition with herbs and capperwort and guarguarisms, and your treatment does not confirm, then you should cauterize the disease with three cauteries: the first on the edge of the ear, the second a little below the temple, and the third at the junction of the two lips.
And pause your cautery according to what is opposite the affected part, for softening occurs only in the part that appears healthy
And the manner of cautery is that you cauterize it with a cautery on the right at the tip of the ear lobe above a little on the horn of the head, and another one on the temple, its length being according to the length of the finger joint, and then pause your hand with the cautery until the amount of the mass of the tumor is consumed.
And this is the manner of cautery, and it is a species of the cutlery, the form of which is flat. But yet more subtle than this one sees is that one which you have here; and it is necessary to cut away in place of superfluous roughness.
And then treat the place with water that is before processed until it is healed
Chapter VII
Of cautery for ancient apoplexy.
When apoplexy is ancient and you treat it with the water we have mentioned and your treatment does not help and there is no fever, then cauterize it with four cauteries: on all of its horns of the head; and a cautery in the middle place of the head, as we have said; and a cautery in the throat. And the manner of cautery is done according to what has been mentioned above
And then cauterize it over the mouth of the stomach; and do this last; and then treat it with water that you have processed.
Chapter VIII
Of cautery for oblivation caused by a rash
It is necessary to give the patient at the beginning large jars and pills of white hellebore.
"Next, shave the head of the patient and place on the cushion of the poultice described in the treatise on poultices."
"And pause from time to time, for this is the manner of cautery." "And do that according to the methodical order which I have already mentioned."
"If it is not healing well like that, then make three cauteries on the last section of his head, which should be decreasing from the most sovereign part of the head towards the neck." "And pause between each cautery for the thickness of a finger, and then carefully cure the cautery with what has been prepared."
"But if you see that the patient is tolerating it well, then make the cautery in the middle of the location; and if you want greater effectiveness, then cauterize those on both ears."
"Carefully cure that until it is healed; and let the cauteries be olive-shaped according to the form given above."

Chapter Nine: Cautery for Paralysis and Softening of the Whole Body
"And when you proceed with the softening of the head using herbs and what has been said; and carefully shave the head of the patient, and then make a cautery in the middle of the head, and cauteries on all the horns of the head, and cauterize the last section of it, and make three cauteries on the cervical vertebrae."
"And if it is necessary to soften the body in a paralysis where the patients tolerate it and the condition is severe, then cauterize that with four cauteries on the vertebrae of the back, and afterwards make a cautery where the muscle of the nape of the neck is fought against, and raise the patient's hand." "And carefully cure it until it is healed, and let this be an olive-shaped cautery."
Capítol deu.
Chapter Ten: Cautery for Epilepsy
"No cautery is made on the epileptic unless the epilepsy is due to phlegm."
"And then you should soften the brain at the beginning of it using herbs and the other treatments which have been mentioned in the division when the patient is large and tolerates the exception of medications."
"And if it is a child who does not tolerate medications, then administer purgatives and mastigators that soften the brain beforehand for many days with proper diet."
"And then carefully shave the head of the patient, and make a cautery in the middle of the head according to the previous manner, and another cautery in the occiput of it, and cauterize each horn of the head." "And if the patient is severe and tolerates it, then cauterize that with the cauteries which have been mentioned, having paralysis and softening of the body on the cervical vertebrae and the dorsal vertebrae."
"And let it be an olive-shaped cautery according to what has been stated before."
"But if the patient is a child, then pause and make a subtle cautery in this manner:"
Capítol undecim.
"Regarding cautery of melancholy."
"When the causes of melancholy are corrupted humidity and thick phlegm, then cauterize with those cauteries that we have mentioned previously."
"And if the cause of melancholy is declining surplus leading to it, and the body of the patient is humid, then let him drink water that cleanses the brain following what has been mentioned in the division."
"And then shave the patient's head, and properly make a wreath of laurel leaves for him to wear on his forehead, and then place it in the middle of his head."
"And let the patient lie on his left side, and let him be held tightly on all parts."
"And then apply a liniment; and afterwards it is fitting to rub with wool grease." "And warm that on the fire for temperate heating according to measure, which he shall suffer when it is more in him." "And then place that in the middle of his head within the crown, and leave it there until it grows cold."
"And do this with the patient once every week until his illness is healed; or if you wish, cauterize him making small punctures according to the extent of the illness, but holding your hand thus ordered with a cautery: this is called 'equal' cautery which moistens the brain evenly."
"And then apply that cataplasm wrapped in wool or in flaxseed."
"Chapter Twelve."
"Of cauterization of descending water in the groin."
"When you have determined the beginning of water descent in the groin by the signs which I have mentioned in the division, then begin and give the patient to drink water that cleanses his head, and guard him from all humidity."
"And keep him warm in bed for several days."
"And then command him to shave his head, and cauterize it with a cautery in the middle of the head; and also cauterize it with two cauteries on both temples if it is the beginning of descent of water from both groins, or on one side only if it is the beginning of descent on one side."
"Cauterize with a cautery all the veins and arteries that are near the shoulder blade; and let the cauteries be in this length at the latitude of the temples."
"And guard against fluxes of blood when he is being cauterized; and if you see any flux of blood, stop it with some medicine which is at your disposal."
"And I will come with skill to extract arteries and cut them off and to care for fluxes of blood."
"Sometimes it is cauterized on the neck near the two bones with two cauteries running downwards."
"Chapter Thirteen."
"Of cauterization for old tears."
"When tears from the eyes are old and abundant, and it is verified that this is due to superfluous phlegmatic humors in the veins and arteries which are at the manifest location of the head outside, then cauterize him with a cautery as we have described in the chapter on the beginning of descending water in the groins, and also with a cautery in the middle of the head and with two cauteries on the neck near the two temples, and with two cauteries on the neck near the two bones." "And if you need to add something more, then cauterize him on both sides of the cheekbone above the eyebrow with small cauteries."

"Of cauterization for foul breath from the nose."

"And also cauterize him with a small cautery and two cauteries on both eyebrows near the hair, a little below them."
"Be careful not to burn the artery."

"Chapter Fifteen."
"Concerning the cauterization for the softening of eyelids of eyes."
"When an eyelid becomes softened by illness or moisture, cauterize that eyelid with this lunar cautery; and this is its form:"
"And if you wish to cauterize above the two eyebrows a little with two cauteries on each side, they should be elongated from the temples." "And the length of each cautery should be according to the quantity of the eyebrow."

Chapter Sixteen
"Concerning cautery of the eyelid when the hairs are converted into parts within and piercing the eye."
"When the hairs of the eye are converted into parts within so that they pierce the eye, cauterize in those places either with fire or with medicated cautery."
"If cauterizing with fire, command the patient beforehand that he pluck his hairs like those which they usually pluck, until they are lengthened and hardened; and if it pierces there, then you should stretch the eyelids of it with a bandage so that no harm comes to them until the hairs have grown."
"And when they have grown long and hardened, then pause the head of the patient in the usual position, and approximate a tent over the eyelid of the eye with fire, shaped like the leaf of a spear, and let the beginning of it be close to the hairs."
"And then pause with cotton dipped in alum or in mucus of pigeon over the eye."
"And then light the cautery which is of this shape."
"And then cauterize little by little along the figure which is outlined, with small glances, until the surface of the chain which is like the leaf of myrtle is burned."
"And the sign of the good work is that you see the eyelid of the eye already contracted and its hairs raised from the puncture of the eye."
"And then elevate your hand and leave it for three days, and then pause cotton on the border until the scar is healed." "And then dress that with ointment until it is healed."
"But if the hairs return for some cause after their growth and the eyelid becomes softened, then perform the cautery again over that just as you had done originally."
"But if the hairs remain on the eyelid, then cauterize them until they are lifted up to their natural place and hardened, so that they do not pierce the eye."
"But when cauterizing with medicinal fire, this is what you command the patient: pluck the hairs until they are lengthened and hardened; then make from cloth paper the shape of a myrtle leaf."
"And then take three ounces of known soap and three ounces of quicklime, mix those causes well, make haste so that it does not cool down; then spread this on the cloth which is made like the shape of a myrtle leaf, and place it over one eye or both eyes. Then place cotton dipped in alum over the eye, and hold the patient's head in position."
"And then pause your finger on the medicine and press it gently without moving until the patient feels the bite of the medicine, for the bite is like that of fire."
"And then when the patient perceives that bite, then remove the medicine and move it with your finger; then when the bite ceases, then remove the medicine and wash the eye with water. And then consider if perhaps the eyelid is lifted up like when washed by the constriction with fire or incision; for then it is well done. But if not, return to that of the medicine on the place where it has not adhered, do not denigrate until the operation is hardened and the eye is contracted."
"And then pause cotton on the border until the chain of adhesion is eradicated; then dress that with ointment of definicon or with another one until it is healed."
"And it is necessary that you, due to your operation, guard with vigilant diligence that no dust of the medicine falls into the eye; and if the eyelid becomes softened during some days and for some cause hairs pierce the eye, then repeat your medicine on that place where the eyelid is softened, just as you did at the beginning; then surround it until it is healed."
"And this is the form of myrtle leaf."
"And know that the eyes of men are diversified according to their magnitude and smallness; and therefore your constriction is made accordingly."
"And do not hide the way of rectitude from those who study this art."
Chapter XVII.
On cauterization of a fistula that is in the lachrymal duct of the eye.
"When treating a fistula as mentioned in the sections on diseases and your treatment does not succeed, then you should cauterize it in this manner: tell the patient to hold their head steady with their hands, and have one of your assistants press their head gently but firmly between their hands."
"And also apply a poultice made of hot water or mustard plasters on the affected area."
"And next, prepare the cauterization instrument, which is shaped like this:"
"This [cautery] should be hollow, like a pipe or the quill of an eagle, with one end through which cauterization is performed."
"And if desired, let it be penetrating into the other end as well." If you wish it to come out as it was inserted.
But that which is concave is better for this task.
"And then press the fistula if it is open, and draw out the fluid and dry that area." "And if it's not open, make an incision there and extract the pus from it."
"And then press the cautery, which should be well ignited, onto that area, but be careful not to touch the patient's skin too much near the nostrils so as not to cause error or discomfort for them. Then place the cautery on the grey hairs of the beard and burn them."
"And if at the beginning of your cautery it enters into the bone, that's good. And if not, then repeat the cautery once or twice if necessary. Then leave that area alone for three days, and afterwards press on it with a border and around it with a drying ointment until it is healed."
"But if eleven days have passed and it has not healed, then apply a corrosive medication to it until the bone is exposed and it is scraped according to what is convenient in its chapter."
"And here is another method of cauterizing a fistula that some first said: enter into the location of the fistula and make an incision there with a subtle needle whose shape is like this. Then place in that fissure the amount of one inch of melted lead; then place your hand on it with good retention, so that no harm comes to the patient so that the melted lead does not reach the skin of that area; and cover the area of the patient's skin around it wrapped in white album or water, because lead hardens the location of the fistula and heals it by marvelous healing."
"And if the fistula is healed with what we have said about cauterization and treatment, that's good. And if not, then it is necessary to administer a traction of the nose and reduce the fistula into the body of the nose according to what will come in its proper place."

Chapter XXI
Of cautery of toothache.
When toothache is caused by coldness or there's ice or worm inside it, or if the cure does not succeed with medicine, then cauterize that one in two ways: either with a red-hot iron from the fire or with a hot coal.
To cauterize with a red-hot iron: Take an iron and heat it in the fire, then quickly grasp its end with tongs and touch it to the aching tooth until it becomes hot.
And repeat this several times until the heat of the fire reaches the root of the teeth.
And if you wish, first immerse wool or cotton in the aforementioned hot coal, then place it on the aching tooth and hold the red-hot iron close to it until it reaches the cavity of the tooth.
But be careful when using fire for cautery, so that the coal or iron is not too hot and does not burn the mouth of the patient.
Then shape the coal or iron as desired, place it on the tooth and hold your hand close until it becomes cool. Repeat this several times until the pain ceases, either that same day or the next day.
And it's necessary for the patient to hold their mouth open on that side after this cautery, keeping it closed tightly for an hour, and then spit out the saliva. This is how the cautery should be performed.
You may perform the cautery with whichever method you prefer, depending on what you find easiest to do.

Chapter Twenty-two
On the cautery of hernias.
When hernias are caused by mucus and humors that are not easily digested despite medication, then cauterize them using this method: Take two tubes made of horn or metal, attach them to the cautery, and place it over the swelling. And if the swelling is small, then apply the cautery according to its size, and leave it on for three days. Then remove it and press a cloth soaked in warm water onto the affected area until what was burned by the fire is removed.
And then treat that wound with ointments, bandages, and dressings until it heals.

"And especially raise your hand with the instrument and wipe away all of the cold water from around the hip joint with fresh water."
"And especially leave it alone for three days and then place border paste on it until the blackness of the adhering cautery is removed, leaving it like that for a few days more, and then rub some ointment on it; this is the last stage of treatment."
"And especially treat it with ointment until it is healed."
"And if the pain extends to the thigh or the buttock, do as was done for the hip joint, containing water as described."
"This is the method of cold water application, which I have already written about in my treatise on the correction of medicines." "And place another bowl inverted on top of that bowl, and pour through it some warm water over the alkali and quicklime until they are covered by about one finger's depth; then press them firmly with your hand, and leave the bowl containing the cold water to drain into the inverted bowl below."
"And especially adjust all that water and pour it over some fresh slaked lime and alkali again, because this solution will be very strong and is used in many medical operations and cauterizations of other members."
"And some medicines are used for cauterizing broad areas, such as those containing turmeric and honey with the addition of vinegar and soap so that they are mixed together."
"And Galen tells of an ancient man who was cured by one session of cauterization for pain in the hip and sciatic nerve, and he greatly praised this treatment saying that no other cure is needed because it brought about healing in one session as told."

"Next, take a dry goat's hoof and heat it in the fire until it becomes hot. Then place it on wool or linen that has been spread out." "And repeat this until the sensation of the bite reaches the ankle and relieves the pain."
"This method of cautery is called cautery of oxen."

"Chapter XLv."
"Of cautery of fractures."
When there is fracture in the bones or displacement of the intestines before the animal's anus, and when this begins to happen, then you must order the patient to refrain from food on that day and to use gentle laxatives so that the wound may heal more easily.
And then place the patient between your hands on their back, and command them to hold their breath while you feel for the anus or the intestines.
And then return with your hands to where you said and try to feel the fracture on the ribs with the tip of your finger, signaling which end is like half of a circle facing upwards.
And then perform the cautery as follows:
"Until it becomes moist and releases sparks." "And then gently reduce the intestine or hernia to its cavity, and place your hand over the area to ensure that it does not come out again."
"And you have already placed yourself between the patient's thighs and placed a cushion under them, with other servants on their legs, and another on their chest, holding their hands."
"And then place the cautery on that spot with your right hand, and bring the intestine towards the opening of the wound, ensuring that you grasp the edge of the opening; repeat this process until you have successfully grasped it."
"And carefully observe the condition of the intestine during cauterization, making sure that you do not burn it so that the patient does not come to harm or suffer great injury."
"And know that if you do not grasp [the intestine] with the cautery, your operation is incomplete."
"It is necessary that the cautery used for children be thin according to their age and size."
"And then clean the wound from the cautery with warm water three times a day until the scar from the burn has healed."
"And then treat it with other remedies until it is healed."
"And the patient should remain in bed for forty days until the wound is sealed and the inflammation has subsided."
"It is necessary that you adjust the patient's diet according to the duration of their treatment, so that it does not empty the stomach and cause the intestine to protrude due to the effort of healing."
"And then, when forty days have passed, gradually administer solid food to them, and keep them on this diet for another forty days."
"And they should avoid strenuous work, excessive eating and drinking, and loud voices, as these things will hinder the healing of their wound."
"And now I will speak about the treatment of ruptures in other parts of the abdomen, and if they are not too large, you should cauterize the rupture with a round cautery according to its size, so that it is equal to one third of the width of the intestine; and then treat it with water as we have said."
"And some earlier authors have said that a rupture should be cauterized with a triangular cautery shaped like this: △"
"And a line is placed that runs through the width in the side where it rises from the break, and another line above it; then place your hand with a pointed cautery, but the first cautery should be lighter and better."
"Chapter XLVI."
"Regarding cauterization of a twisted cord."
"When pain occurs in the upper limbs due to cautery or percussion and persists for a long time without being alleviated by medicinal treatment, it is necessary to cauterize with a pointed cautery."
"And let the cautery be of the size of the member according to its magnitude and smallness, and its strength and weakness, and the location of the twist and the pain it causes."
"If it is healed by the first cautery, that is good. And if not, then apply the cautery again; for those pains are often caused by punctures of a member near to where the pain is felt, so it is necessary to reach those with cauteries until the illness is healed."
"Chapter XLVI."
"Regarding cauterization of leprosy."
"Some forms of leprosy are viewed with caution when cauterized because it does not bring much benefit, and even harm if the species of leprosy is caused by putrefaction of phlegm or melancholy."
"And therefore, when you want to cauterize that one, consider whether the leprosy is contagious and affected as we said in the division, and do not do it if it is so. Also fear that the corruption might spread throughout the whole body and affect all its structures. Therefore, cauterize there on the head with five cauteries: one in the middle of the head, and the second below it near the forehead; two on the horns; and one behind on the nape or servants."
"And lastly, press the cautery a little deeper until it makes a small impression on the bone, and remove the scabs from there, so that the expiration of thick vapors is alleviated. And cauterize on the chest as necessary."
"And if the leprosy has already spread over the whole body and appears manifestly, then you must cauterize that one with those cauteries which we have mentioned for the head; and cauterize on the tip of the nose, and with two cauteries on each cheekbone, and with two cauteries on each shoulder blade, and with six cauteries on the vertebrae of the back, and with one large one on the vertebrae near the buttocks, and one on the buttock itself, and with two on each ankle, and with one on each ankle bone, and with two on each shinbone, and with two on each calf muscle; and cauterize there over all the joints of the said limbs and feet, and on each heel of the feet, and on the hollows of the hands."
"And beware not to burn the nerves which are located above the ankle lest you harm them."
"Sometimes it is cauterized with one cautery on the bone of the penis and another on the mouth of the stomach, and another on the liver."
"And know that the more accurately you apply cauteries, the greater the benefit and advantage. And know that the illness does not feel pain from the cautery, as it does with its own sores, because the body of that one is already stunned."
"And it is necessary for the cauteries to be large or small according to the limbs and joints, as has been prescribed with regard to the species of instruments."
"Furthermore, cure the burn with powdered wheat flour mixed with honey and with other remedies until it is healed."
**Capítol XLVIII.**
**Chapter XLVIII. Cauterization for Stupidity.**
When a limb is paralyzed or numb and treated with medicines, oils, and plasters, yet it does not heal, then cauterize that paralyzed limb using irons according to its size or smallness.
And introduce your cautery into the opening of the backbone slightly. Then treat it with ointment until it heals.
And sometimes veins are cauterized that cause weakness in the feet and legs, in the spine, and on both sides of the nerves which nourish that limb; and then the weakness disappears.
But do not presume to do this unless one is knowledgeable in the anatomy of limbs and the exit of nerves throughout the body in motion.
Chapter XLIX
On cauterization of white patches that are disfiguring.
When white patches are old and do not respond to any medicinal ointments, then cauterize over that area with a hot iron slightly according to the quantity of the opening of the backbone so that it may remove the whiteness and change its color.
And afterwards treat that area with a mixture of powdered earth and lentils with rose oil, and leaves of sage, and dove's blood or hen's blood, giving each one part and mixing them all together, and then apply it with a cloth on which some has been placed, and cover the location so that it may heal.
Chapter L
Cautery of the crab (i.e., treatment for gout).
When cancer begins and you want to remove that lump, then cauterize it with a circular cautery in the same way as it is rotated.
And the wise ones say that it should be cauterized with the last cautery in the middle of the spot; but I have not seen this done because I fear that it may ulcerate, and I have seen this happen several times.
And it is then more appropriate to cauterize around the spot with a circular motion as we have said before, or with many cauteries.
Chapter 52
On the cautery of adenitis (swelling of the lymph glands).
When some adenitis is delayed in ripening, and this happens due to superfluity of that area or due to the condition of the illness, as it is old and decrepit with little blood or because of time, and you want to hasten the ripening of the adenitis; then cauterize around it with many small punctures using cauteries; and approach that area which has delayed in ripening.
But if you want to make a puncture with the cautery, then heat the cautery of which this is the shape: and afterwards place that in the middle of the adenitis until it penetrates the cord.
And if the cautery in that area causes too much pain, so that the flesh of the arm is relaxed; then approach and cure it until it is healed.
Chapter 53
On the cautery of corroding ulcers
Corroding is a wandering corruption in the member which consumes it as dry wood burns.
Therefore if you find that corroding in a place where cautery with fire can be applied, then heat cautery nails, some few and some large according to what is suitable for that area where the corroding is.
And approach it cauterizing all around until you have eradicated all corruption and there remains no cause of it left.
And leave that for three days, and apply over the cauterized places only ointment mixed with oil until all scars are eradicated and all corruption is gone.
And then cure it with living flesh applied on it.
But if after three days you find that the flesh is growing healthy without any corruption, then that's good. But if not, then repeat the cautery over what remains in the corrupted places.
And corroding can be treated sometimes with sharp medicine, for it is a halfway measure instead of cautery. But nevertheless, cautery with fire gives quicker relief.
And I have already mentioned the treatment of it by sharp medicine in its division, so take that when you begin to deal with it.
Chapter 54
On cautery of chilblains and similar afflictions
Many times it happens in the parts of the body called chilblains, which is a thick, deep-seated cause that affects the skin. Cautery can be applied to these in two ways: by fire and by hot water.
But cautery with fire is this: heat the cautery like a feather pen made of iron according to the quantity that contains the chilblain entirely, and it should be made of fine edges.
And approach that heated cautery upon the chilblain, and then rotate your hand with the cautery around the circumference of the chilblain until it reaches to the depth of it. Leave it for three days until it begins to discharge water. "Then apply a poultice made of wild mallow leaves chopped with salt, and leave the poultice on that area for one night, as it will draw out its roots."
"And then treat the wound with ointment made from generation flesh until it heals."
"And if it is not converted, and blisters sometimes occur on the surface of the body, especially on the hands and feet, then you should administer cauterization with water, using a spoon made of brass, iron or vulture's feather; place it over the boil; take a drop of boiling water in the spoon, keeping your hand still, press the margin of the spoon onto the root of the boil, allowing the boiling water to reach the center of the root; wait for the patient to endure the bite of the boiling water for about an hour, then remove it, as the boil with its roots will be eradicated."
"And do this until all of those that are on the body have come out."
"And then treat those boils from which the roots of the boils have been eradicated with ointments that cause the flesh to grow again."
Chapter .lxxv.
Of cauterization for trembling.
When trembling occurs due to friction in the nerves or from a fever caused by heat, or from another similar cause, then you should cauterize it with four cauteries or five on the vertebrae of the back, between each vertebra with one cautery; and apply a cautery on their foot, and on their stomach with an olive cautery.
And if the trembling subsides, it will hasten the recovery from the feverish illness.
Chapter .lvi
About cauterization of accidental injuries to the body
When the body is speckled with albati (white spots), and there are pustules from which matter is issuing that is thick and corrupt; therefore, at the beginning, it must be cauterized with a subtle cautery made of myrtle wood, the extremity of which has been heated in fire; or with a long erestological rasp; or with a lenticular cautery.
And similarly, in the case of other boils that appear later, they are cauterized at the beginning of their expulsion according to this manner; and they are not believed, nor are they opened up, but rather the excess is dissipated by doing so, and they heal.
But nevertheless it is necessary that this be done near an evacuation with phlebotomy.
Chapter lvi
About cauterization of accidental flow of blood by incision with an artery knife
There are often cases where an arterial flow appears that is cut through the skin where it has erupted, or from the incision of an apostema or cautery of a member, and then it resembles this, and it is difficult to stop it.
Therefore, when this happens to someone, immediately take your hand with the artery knife and press it over that place where you saw the arterial flow issuing; pause there a little while until you see that the flow of blood has ceased from under your finger, so that it does not escape.
And immediately afterward heat in fire the olive-shaped cauteries of various sizes, whether few or many; and blow upon them until they are very hot.
And then promptly take one of those cauteries that is small or large according to the place and size of the wound in which the artery has burst; apply it there quickly after you have removed your finger, and hold it until it becomes adherent and stops the bleeding.
And if the blood is still issuing from the orifice of the artery when you remove your finger and apply the cautery, then immediately take another one that has been prepared in the fire; and continue to do this until the bleeding has stopped.
And be sure not to burn any nearby nerves, and let it come close to the wound but without causing another mischief.
And know that when blood flows from an artery, it is not possible to stop the bleeding in those cases except by one of four methods: either with cautery as described above, or with extraction if it cannot be extracted (for when it is extracted, the ends of the vessel are burned and the bleeding stops), or else it should be tied with thread or linen by strong traction, or some medicine whose virtue is to stop bleeding should be applied there, and pressed upon with a compress accompanied by constriction.
But those who apply restriction with linen thread and traction with cloths or bandages by positioning cauteries and similar things, do not perform but harm.
But if this happens to someone and the physician is not present nor any medicine, then one should press with the tip of the finger over the orifice of that vein as described above, and apply great constriction of the area around it so that the blood may be stopped from its source; and remove the finger from the artery, and sprinkle water that has been rubbed much with a very cold handkerchief upon the artery so that the blood may be congealed and thickened; and afterwards see if cautery or medicine is necessary.
Of Incision and Perforation and Excision and of Phlebotomy and of Wounds and Their Like.
We have already spoken in the first chapter of all diseases in which cautery with fire is appropriate and with medicine burning, and the occasions and causes for this, and the instruments necessary for them with their forms; and we have arranged the chapters concerning the head down to the feet.
And in this chapter, I will proceed similarly so that what is sought by anyone may be easily understood; therefore regarding whatever question he may ask.
But before I begin this, please note that in this chapter about cutting and perforation, you should understand that it is for terror what was said in the first chapter concerning cautery.
And for this reason, it is necessary that there should be great caution in these operations because many times evacuation takes place with blood, which carries life within itself, such as aspiration of the vein or incision over an aposteme or opening of an abscess or curettage of a wound or extraction of an arrowhead or incision of a stone and their like. And all these are accompanied by fear and trembling, and in many cases death ensues from them.
And I warn you not to fall into something that is doubtful, for sometimes it happens that one must resort to methods that are very dangerous. And among them are some who depart with their disease and it is easy for death to follow upon it; this happens because of the severity of their illness, the duration of it, and fear of that illness which signifies death.
And among them is he who gives away all his property and possessions in expectation of health but whose disease is fatal.
Therefore, do not consent to anyone who comes to you with this manner; let your caution be greater than greed and rapacity. And do not undertake any cause without first having certain scientific knowledge that will verify the matter for you, and towards which successful outcome may be hoped.
And use prognosis and diagnosis of that which leads to health in the treatment of all your diseases; for therein lies help towards acquiring fame and renown, praise and glory.
O children, may God inspire you with His understanding and not remove direction and protection from you; for this is in His hand.
And I have arranged this chapter divided into chapters according to what has been said in the chapter on cautery, from the treatment of the head down to the feet, so that you may easily understand what you ask about and what you need.
First Chapter.
Of the Treatment of Water in the Head of Children
Know that this disease often happens to children at birth, especially when the midwife squeezes too hard on the head of the child while it is being born.
And sometimes it happens without any apparent cause which cannot be discovered.
But I have only seen this disease in children; and all those whom I saw died from it, and therefore it seems to me that it is not an easy task to deal with such cases.
I have seen an infant whose head was filled with water and his head swelled so much that he could not raise himself because of the greatness of his head; and more than this humidity caused death.
And this water is collected either between the dura mater (dural membrane) and the bone, or outside the bone on top of the skull.
For if the operation is performed in such a case where the water is between the dura mater and the bone, and the swelling is small, then you should make an incision at the middle of the head with a scalpel horizontally, and let its length be about two fingers so that the water may flow out through it, for this is the form of the spatula:

**Chapter VI.**
**On the treatment of what falls into the ears.**
All causes that enter the ears are of four kinds: for it is either a mineral stone or a cause similar to stone, such as iron and copper; or it is of plant origin like chickpeas or beans; or it is a fluid cause like water, vinegar and their like; or some animal.
Therefore, when a stone enters the ear or another cause similar to those causes that do not fit nor enter into the ear, and it stops the ear's opening, if sometimes it moves the stone, then it distills in that certain amount of oil violet or sesame, and properly administer its extraction from there, and make it sneeze with conditions, and close the nose because of the arrival of sneezing. And properly plug in the ear with some pieces of cloth or wool, and stretch the ear upwards to avoid these causes being forgotten.
And if it is not gotten rid of, then properly administer its extraction using the instrument called "gutter catheter" of which this is the form:
And if it is forgotten with the instrument, that's good. But if not, then properly administer its extraction using a soft hook of little duplication.
And therefore if it is not removed by that, then make a tube of silver and insert the extremity of the tube into the opening of the ear and close around the tube with wax and softened oil so that only the tube may be inserted. And properly extract it using a small bellows with strong suction, for often times with this method that we have described.
But if it is not removed in this manner, then take some salted alum or sometimes prepared with which birds are caught by taking a small quantity of it, and place it at the end of the ear, and properly wrap that well-placed spot decently. And properly insert it into the opening of the ear with ease, and properly dry out the ear from any moisture.
And therefore if it is not removed by all the causes that we have described, then you should cut that in front before an abscess or spasm occurs.
And the manner of cutting that is that you first sanctify the vein sepsis and extract the blood according to the method of its virtue, and then make that cut between your thumbs and turn the ear upwards, and finish with a small incision in the root of the ear where the grease of it is pressed. And let the incision be crescent-shaped so that it reaches to the ear's lobe. And when the lobe is hardened, remove it if possible with appropriate instruments; and then quickly sew up the incision at that time, and care for it until it heals.
And if the cause of pain in the ear is one of the hairs that grew and became inflamed, then administer its treatment and extraction. But if it does not obey your attempt at examination, then you take a fine, thin spatula according to this form: And use that spatula to perform the excision of that hair which has fallen into the ear.
And do not perform this when you think that the hair has already been moistened by the vapor of the ear. Rather, place it in small pieces and then extract them with tweezers or gentle movements, or through excision as mentioned earlier, because the extraction is facilitated by these methods.
But when water enters the ear, it is necessary that the patient sneeze at the beginning and fill their ear with a little cotton wool. Then place it on that ear in which there is water, and if through this method it is removed, then good. But if not, then take some thin lead pipes and make them red-hot over fire, and the patient inserts one of those into the opening of his ear, pressing one side of it against that part and striking another pipe with a hammer onto the one that is inside the ear. And do not cease this until all the water has been removed.
And do not cease this until all the water has been removed. And if the water is not thus removed, then you take some paper or cotton, and place one end of it into the ear while extending the other end over fire until most of it is burnt.
And then place another cotton and do this several times until all the water has been removed. Then remove it with a cannula as described above of the ear extractor.
But in the extraction of a beast entering that ear, if it is a small creature such as a flea or its like, cure it in the same way as we have described in the division. But if it is a large creature which causes discomfort to the sense of hearing, then administer its extraction with gentle movements and tweezers. And the cause of this is easier than all other causes that occur in the ear.
But in the extraction of a worm generated in the ear, when you cure it with what we have said in the division and treatise of distillations and yet do not succeed, then you must examine the ear in sunlight.
And if any cause of worms is seen here, then extract it with gentle movements or with fine tweezers. But if no such cause appears, then take a cannula made of bronze that is narrow at its base and wide at its top, shaped like this: And insert the fine end of this cannula into the ear according to what it can bear. Then suck with it strongly and do this many times until all the worms are removed.
But if it does not obey your examination, then fill and close the circuit of the cannula with wax as we have said. Then administer distillations which are already proven in the treatment of worms, as you will find in the treatise on distillations.
And this is the shape of the instrument with which you should administer medicinal oils into the ear: Made of silver or brass, narrow at its base and having a small opening, and flat on top.
And let it be shaped in such a way that it fits into the concavity of the cannula where it will be necessary to apply this. "If you wish, take the wand and wrap it gently around the end of the patient's thigh. Capítulo VII
On the treatment of ear infections.
It sometimes happens that some children are born from their mothers' wombs without perforations in their ears, and this has also happened to some men. This can cause infection inside the ear due to water or flesh trapped there; sometimes this infection appears at the entrance of the ear canal and does not allow for proper cleaning, and other times it appears on the outer parts of the ear.
And that which happens at the entrance of the ear canal, which cannot be cleaned out easily, is usually the most difficult to treat.
But in those cases where you can see inside the ear, it is necessary for you to hold the patient's ear up to the sun and observe carefully. And if an accumulation of pus appears, then open that with a fine spatula, whose shape is like this:
If the extremity where width is desired has one sharp end and the other blunt, and the spatula has two sides Lion-like to prevent injury to the ear.
Then if the operation is performed on bare skin of the ear or face, at that time you should use fine sharp scissors and cut through that tissue with great ease until all the skin has been removed.
And if the operation is on the front of the ear, then take a thin Lion's claw, heat it in the fire for a moment, and promptly insert it into the flesh of the ear.
And therefore if you perform an operation with water where the illness appears easily, for fear of heaviness, relieve the pressure with ease; and be careful not to harm the nerves of the ear.

Chapter IX

Chapter X.
On the treatment of a boil on the upper eyelid of the eye
A boil is a swelling that occurs in the tissues of the upper eyelid, especially in children, and it causes inflammation of the eyes and often affects their sight because tears are secreted abundantly from them.
Therefore those children keep their heads constantly down and also sleep with them down; and therefore the eyelids of theirs below become humid and swollen, which is already covered by inflammation, and the presence of a boil is about to appear in the eye; and when you press the place with your fingers, you feel hardness within it.

And be sure not to insert the scalpel into the incision, lest you damage the eye and harm it.

Chapter XXII
Of the treatment of corneal ulcers

And therefore you should cut it at the beginning of its appearance and remove all of it. Then pause there with fire or cautery or some burning medicine which is applied to that place.
If its incision is delayed until it becomes magnificent, then consider if it is hardened, hard, of dark color and with little sensation, then do not touch that with iron for it is a cancerous ulcer; for many times those who incise this ulcer end up doing great harm to the one they had intended to help.
And if the ulcer is of lion-like touch and not dark in color, and sometimes incision is possible throughout that area, then evacuate the patient and incise without fear, and dress the wound with something that dries and constrains until it heals.
Chapter XXVI
On the suturing of the nose, lips, and ear when continuity has been lost due to plague or injury.
Know that when such a solution of continuity occurs in one of these cartilages, little confidence should be placed in that operation by certain men.
Therefore, when it happens to someone that there is some cause of these, consider if it is fresh plague with its blood, and then you should approximate the two lips of the wound with sutures, and afterwards dress it so that it heals.
And if the lips of the solution of continuity are already separated and each is healthy, then you should cut off each part of its apparent connection until there comes out no blood. And then approximate the two lips with sutures and strengthen them, and over those sprinkle dragon's blood powder and a little incense, and place on top of it a piece of plaster made from diachylon or some other consolidative plaster, leaving it like that for two days or three, then remove it and change the plaster, allowing the wound to heal by itself. Afterwards dress it with ointment until it is healed.
But the manner of suturing is that you approximate the solution of continuity either with needles as we have recommended in the suturing of the belly, or with thread as you know how to do.
Chapter XXVII
Of the extraction of those causes that appear between the two lips in wounds.
Frequently it happens to many men that in the wounds of their lips there appear hard abscesses resembling boils of ears, some small and others larger.
It is necessary to convert each of those hardnesses by turning the lips and splitting them open with a sharp tool, then fill the space with sage steeped in wine until blood clots, wash it with vinegar, then dress the wound with an astringent so that it heals.
Chapter XXVIII
Of the incision of attached skin on the gums.
If a granuloma appears on the attached gum, which they used to call an albulus, you should suspend it with tweezers or hold it with your fingers and incise it in its entirety, allowing the pus to flow out and the blood to coagulate.
And then apply sage steeped in wine or other astringent powders or ointments to the wound.
And if that skin returns again, you should incise it once more and cauterize it with a hot iron, for then it will not return.
Chapter XXIX
"Due to iron teeth."
"If on the surface of the teeth between the interdental spaces and those in front, as well as between the gums, rough, sharp, and sometimes blackish scales appear, with green or yellowish-yellow color seen through the gum, this is a sign of decay and the teeth are loose."
"And therefore you should seize the patient between your hands and place their head in a cloth tie, and scrape the teeth on which those scales appear and cause similar sand-like grains to appear without causing any damage, and this is due to the blackness and yellowness and other discolorations."
"So if this is the end of that which was at the beginning of the reason, well then. And otherwise, you should repeat the reason on those another day and again on the third day until it comes to the final statement in that which you want."
"And know that teeth require various types of tools with different shapes and forms according to what is prepared for your operation." "And therefore take the tool with which you scrape the tooth from its interior and know that it is different from the tool with which you scrape between teeth according to other forms. And these forms of tools should be prepared by you, as you will see soon."
"Chapter XXX."
"Tooth extraction."
"The cause of toothache and its pain is due to the harmful humour that corrupts it. When this humour is eradicated, there is no reason why the toothache should persist, for it is a subtle substance that causes pain during eradication."
"Therefore, when a patient comes to have a tooth extracted, you must be firmly assured which is the aching tooth. For often the pain seems to come from another place and you extract one while the pain continues until the diseased tooth has been removed."
"So when you are certain which tooth is aching, then you should scrape around it with a spatula having some virtue until it has dissolved from the gum completely. Then remove it with your fingers or fine forceps gradually until it comes loose."
"Then take large forceps for good grasp or strong pressure and hold the head of the patient between your thumbs so that he does not move it. Then extract the tooth straightly so that you neither break it nor cause greater pain."
"And if it has not come out yet, then take one of those instruments and place it on the outside of the root with ease and force to facilitate removal as was done at the beginning."
"But if the tooth is decayed or rotten, then you must fill that decay with wax and strengthen it with a thin wire at its extremity so that it does not break when you grasp it with forceps."
"And you must work carefully with your scalpel around the entire gum and guard your strength so that you do not break it nor cause it to separate from its root. Then return to the patient because sometimes the second pain is greater than the first."
"And beware of doing what many ignorant barbers do in their haste and audacity to extract teeth without administering what we have recommended. For often they cause great illnesses upon men which are harder to treat than the tooth itself, and sometimes they leave behind roots or pieces of them, or even extract a tooth with some bones from the jawbone as we have often witnessed."
"And when extracting it, wash the mouth with hot vinegar or vinegar and salt."
"And if there are flows of blood from this, as often happens, then take some quantity of sage and sprinkle it on the wound. If the bleeding does not stop, cauterize it."
"The form of the forceps and fine tweezers with which you should grasp the tooth at the beginning should be long in their extremities, short in handle, and thick so that they do not bend when working with them."
"And they should be like tongs with a thick handle within which, when you squeeze them, they are not bent. Their extremities should be short."
"And they should be made of Indian steel, straight in their extremities. In the extremities of these there should be teeth which interlock with each other and squeeze by descending force. Sometimes the extremities of these are shaped like the beak of a bird called 'ciconia,' that is to say, they are narrow and have great constricting power."
