"Chapter XXXII."
"Of the treatment of prominent teeth above the others."
"When teeth are prominent beyond their natural shape, especially in women and even more so in venerable elderly women. Therefore you should consider: if the tooth is next to another tooth and it cannot be corrected with medication or a splint, then extract that tooth; but if it is not attached to another tooth, then cut that one with this instrument whose shape is like this: it resembles a pig's snout and should be made of Indian steel with a very sharp tip."
"And your incision should be made over three days so that it does not cut into other teeth due to the hardness of the tooth."
"And if a prominent tooth is extracted by grinding, then grind it with an Indian steel file whose shape is like this:"
"And it should be made of Indian steel and very sharp-edged. And its ends should be made with many small points like the teeth of a comb, with which the tooth is ground little by little over several days with ease, so that other teeth are not cut or damaged." "And finally polish it off and remove it with tweezers."
"And if it is a tooth from which one part is broken and it hurts the tongue, then you should grind that edge until its sharpness is smoothed out and flattened so that the tongue does not hurt or speech is not impaired."
"Chapter XXXIII."
"Of restoring broken teeth with gold or silver foil."
"When teeth are broken by concussion and removal due to impact or falling, and the patient cannot eat because of it, and you have treated them with astringent medicines but your treatment has not been effective, then for those that are held together with gold foil and not silver foil, since silver tarnishes quickly and may corrode within a few days, but gold never changes."
"And the foil should be so subtle and thin according to the amount that can fit between the teeth. And the method of attachment is this: take the foil and take twice as much between two healthy teeth, and then curve it with two twists of the foil between the broken ones, or more if there are many, until the foil reaches the other half of the tooth." "And then repeat the wrapping until you reach the beginning of the broken part. Do this with your hand with ease and skill so that it is not further broken."
"And your tying should be done between the roots of the teeth so that it does not slip out."
"And then cut off the excess ends of the foil with forceps or scissors, and press them together in each place with gesture. And turn them over and hide them between the healthy tooth and the broken one so that they do not cause injury to the tongue." "And leave it like this for three days."
"But if it becomes loosened or broken, then fasten it again with more foil in the same manner at all times."
"And this is the form of the teeth and the figure of the correction of two healthy teeth and two broken ones, as shown in these drawings:"
"And when it happens that one or two teeth return to their places after falling, and have been restored as we have recommended, but they become loose again."
"This is done only by skilled and knowledgeable artisans."
"And sometimes it is appropriate to use bone from cattle for this purpose. It should be fashioned in the shape of teeth and placed in the location where the tooth is missing, and fastened as we have said, and it remains and serves for a long time."
"Chapter XXXIV."
"Of cutting the frenulum that comes on the tongue and inhibits speech."
"This ligament which lies beneath the tongue sometimes is natural to some people or occurs accidentally and happens due to a hardened plaque."
"The operation consists of opening the patient's mouth while his head is tilted back. Then raise his tongue and cut that nerve ligament according to its width until the tongue is freed from its attachment."
"But if there is hardness or toughness in that ligament and this has occurred due to hardened plaque, then take an iron nail and cut it lengthwise until you have incised the ligament and dissolved the toughness."
"And be careful not to make a wound in the front of the flesh, and cut here carefully so that there is no blood flow."
"And then rinse the incision site with warm water or vinegar or hot water, and then place a piece of linen beneath the tongue. This is the method that should be used to hold the patient's tongue in place each night so that it does not become hardened again."
"But if there is bleeding, place a wet piece of gauze on the site. But if it continues to bleed, then cauterize the site with a silver nitrate stick which should be used for this purpose." "And then treat it according to the other causes until it is healed."
"Chapter XXXV."
"Of removing a ranula from beneath the tongue."
"Sometimes it happens that under the tongue there is an accumulation resembling a small boil which prevents the tongue from moving naturally, and when it grows large, it fills up the mouth."
"The operation consists of opening the patient's mouth while he is facing the sun and examining the accumulation."
"If you find it to be of ash-gray or blackish hue, hard, when the patient lacks sensation, then do not touch that part as it is gangrenous."
"If it is declinated towards whiteness and humidity, then insert the onion into it, and cut that thin skin, cutting it completely; if blood comes out at the time of your operation, then stop quickly, using vinegar as astringent, so that the blood may be restrained."
"And finally, return to your work until you have completed it, ensuring that the wound is washed with vinegar and salt; then apply the other cure with water until it heals."
"Chapter XXXVI."
"Of the extraction of an abscess from both ears and that which is located in the navel, and of other abscesses."
"When a swelling occurs in the navel area, these are glands which accumulate at times, and when they occur externally, they are called 'ears,' which when cured with water as we have said in the division and it is not healed, then consider whether the abscess is hard, ash-gray in color, with little sensation, then do not touch that part with iron."
"And if it is red in color and the root is large, then do not touch that part with iron because of the flow of blood. Let it remain until it ripens, and then you will remove it yourself or it will break open by itself."
"And if it is white in color, hard, and its root is thin, then that one should be incised."
"And the operation on it is that you consider whether the abscess has already rested and been filled with matter or if it has decreased somewhat. Then do the cutting before sunrise, with the head of the patient lying down and his mouth open, and let the surgeon take between his hands and press the tongue of the patient gently with a very fine instrument, which is shaped thus:"
"And it should be made of silver or bronze and should be thin like a scalpel."
"Then when you press on the tongue with that instrument and the abscess is revealed to you, cut on it lightly at first, then grasp it with forceps and put it in the pan of water, and pull it outward as much as possible." "After that, if you tear any skin, then immediately cut on it with this instrument which is shaped thus:"
"After that, if you tear any skin, then immediately cut on it with this instrument which is shaped thus:" "And it resembles forceps, but its ends are curved so that the tip of each is directed towards the other, very sharp, made of iron with a copper coating."
"But if this instrument is not available to you, then cut with a scalpel which has the following shape: it should be sharp on one side and not sharp on the other."
"And after you have cut one abscess, then cut the other according to this same manner of cutting, and immediately wash out the wound with warm water."
"But if there is a flow of blood, wash it with water decocted from marjoram leaves or myrtle leaves and similar remedies for stopping bleeding until the flow of blood ceases, and then dress the wound until it heals."
"And sometimes other abscesses appear around those two ear openings, and cut them according to what I have said regarding the incision of two equal abscesses."
"And I had previously treated a woman who had an abscess which had appeared in her groin area, which was dark in color and without sensation, having closed the opening of it, and she was breathing with great difficulty and had been prohibited from eating and drinking water, and if there had not been some intervention on that day or the next, she would have died."
"And the abscess had grown so much that it had broken through two places and issued forth through two tracks."
"So I treated her surgically and remained at one of those places, and drew that out, but it was such a large piece that it could not be entirely removed. Then I cut into the place where I understood the other track to be, and immediately opened her mouth, pressed her tongue, and placed forceps on that abscess."
"And then you cut away a large part of it, and there was only a little blood flowing from it." "Therefore the woman's groin was completely healed, and she began drinking water immediately, then took food. And I continued cutting that abscess many times over a long period, but another abscess kept appearing in its place, which cut into the same track."
"So I went away and cauterized her groin with a hot iron, so that there would be no further addition of it. And then I wandered around and did not know what God had done for her on my account."
"Chapter XXXVII."
"Of the incision of the uvula when it is abscessed."
"When catarr descends to the uvula and it becomes abscessed and elongated, then it is called 'penduncle'; but if it is thick and round at its base, then it is called 'bubble'."
"But when it is cured with what we have said in the division and its cure does not confer, sometimes it happens that an abscess which has already cauterized remains there and is subtle. Then you should cut into the one that is attached roundly; and if it is of that length, and is bleeding, of dark color or black, and without sensation, then you should be cautious about cutting it, for there is fear concerning its illness."
"And when you find it according to the manner that I have described regarding its whiteness and length, then make an incision into the illness and press its tongue with this instrument whose shape is thus: and then place forceps on the new one, pull that downwards, and cut into it with one of these instruments which are mentioned in the incision of two abscesses."
"And you should not cut into it any more than what is appropriate to its natural term without addition, for if you cut into it more, you will harm its speech."
"And during the incision, use what we have recommended in the incision of two abscesses, and dress it until it heals."
"But if the illness is frightened by its incision, then you should use a hot iron in its cauterization without fear, and the manner of cauterizing it is not other than with sharp water. And this is how you do it: take the head of the illness in your left hand, press its tongue with the instrument which we have mentioned, take some of the water which we have mentioned in the chapter on cauterization, convey it with that live cause, and pause it on neither thick nor subtle [skin], and with that fill up the concavity of this instrument whose shape is thus:"
"The exterior of that concavity in which the medicine is placed should be like the concavity of a spoon's back, and place the instrument with the medicine on the uvula, so that the illness may turn towards its own side so that no saliva or mucus from the mouth descends through the concave medicine onto the groin area."
"And then place your hand on the medicine and press it on the uvula for half an hour until you see that it has become blackened and softened by the biting of the medicine."
"And if you wish, take cotton and wrap it around the extremity of the ray, immerse the cotton in the medicine, insert the ray with the cotton into a cannula made from over until the cotton adheres to that cannula. Do this several times until you achieve what you desire regarding cauterization of the uvula, then leave it alone for three or four days."
If you need to repeat the medicine, do so, and then cleanse the cauterization around the vein with a hot iron wrapped in wool, modify the area of the medicine with that water, wash it with warm water, and dress it outside with an ointment, and afterwards with bandages until it is healed.
This type of treatment was considered successful for many years due to fear.
Sometimes the uvula is cured with a substance so subtle that it cauterizes and incises, because it heals by means of fumigation in this manner: take calamentum, hyssop, origanum, ruta, scicados arabici, camomilla, bruyera and similar herbs of these kinds, and adjust all or some of them in a vessel, and let them soak in sour wine and boil; and the vessel should be well sealed with clay, and placed in the middle of the vessel is a tripod over which is placed a perforated funnel made of silver or brass.
And the extremity should be inserted into the mouth of the patient until the steam reaches the uvula, so that it can soften and loosen it.
And repeat this treatment several times until it is dry, but be careful not to do this at the onset of an inflammation, as it would irritate the inflammation too much. Instead, you should declare the inflammation with the cauterization.
But if this instrument is not at your disposal, then you should take a reed and fit its extremity with a close of wool, so that the mouth of the patient can be covered. Because the close of wool prevents the steam from burning the mouth.
And this treatment is good for health.
Chapter .xxxviii
Of the extraction of splinters and of that which adheres in the throat, and of other causes.
Many times adhesions are seen in the groin or spine of the foot or some other cause.
Therefore, you must extract that which is apparent from among those [adhesions], over which the sight falls, because when you press the tongue with an instrument before the sun, it will be declared to you what is in the groin.
And that which is not apparent and is hidden in the groin, you must make the patient vomit before the food has digested in the stomach, because it easily removes the cause attached to the groin if forgotten by vomiting; or else let the patient swallow a piece of bread dipped in oil or lettuce juice or a mouthful of dry bread; or take a piece of sea sponge soaked in lion's bile and tie that strongly with fennel, and make the patient swallow it, because when it reaches the place where its spines are extracted, they will be forgotten. And more: take an eel and tie it with fennel and let it be inside the patient, and suddenly extract it; or else take a sieve and suddenly place it [on the groin], and suddenly remove it.
Moreover, if those causes which we have mentioned are not forgotten from there, then use an instrument of lead in this way:
And let it be bigger than a small pea, and at its end have a concavity which you can easily insert into the groin.
"The physician shall raise the patient's head upwards and ensure that no contact is made between the patient's mouth and throat, lest it lead to coughing or spitting out of bones or spine, or that which the physician touches with his hand."
However, if the patient happens to swallow it better, then through his knowledge of the location and cause of the obstruction, he should make him cough downwards and pull out his hand along with the instrument upwards, all according to the quantity that was previously prepared so that none is forgotten.
Chapter XXXIX
Of removing blood clots from the throat.
When bloodsucking has been treated with what we have said in the division on cure with medicines and it does not help, then consider the hours of the day when the throat of the patient is towards the sun, because you should have prepared the tongue of it with the instrument that we have mentioned.
Therefore, if you find a blood clot, remove it gently with tweezers or with skillful movements using your fingers.
And if it is not possible for you to remove it in that way, then take a concave cannula and insert it into the throat of the patient, and place within the concavity of the cannula an iron wire heated red hot, and do this several times (until the blood clot dies and leaves the throat), and afterwards withhold from the patient water all day.
And then take a bladder full of warm water, and place the mouth of it over his mouth, and wash his mouth with that; and do not let any cause him to swallow, for blood clots hate water.
But if it is forgotten what we have mentioned, then fumigate the patient with incense or asafetida through the instrument which we have mentioned in the fumigation of the uvula.
Do this until it passes.
And another method of operation in fumigation of it is that you take an earthenware pot in which there are burning coals and the pot is covered with a lid in the middle of which there is a tube, and the extremity of the instrument is placed in that tube; and then give the fumigation from above; and place the patient's mouth at the extremity of the cannula, and close his mouth so that the fumigation does not escape until you know that the fumigation has reached the blood clot, for the blood clot will soon fall.
And if it does not fall, then repeat the fumigation many times, and withhold from the patient water to drink, and let him eat salty foods and hot ones, and do not let him drink water, and this regimen must be observed for a few days.
And this is the form of the instrument with which blood is removed from the throat when it is seen; and it resembles forceps thus much, except that it has some curvature: which is placed in the throat, and its extremity resembles the beak of an ibis, which is blunt, so that when it takes hold of something, it does not let go.
Chapter XL.
In this chapter is the summary of what has been said about incisions and punctures of abscesses and their openings.
Abscesses are many species, of many kinds, according to the memory of them in this book.
And they are diverse in incision and puncture of them by two methods, one of which is for the species of internal abscesses, and by that which we understand about humidity.
And the second method is for those places where accidents of the body occur, for an abscess that occurs in the head is different from one that occurs in the buttocks; and an abscess that occurs in a fleshy place is different from one that occurs at a joint; and each has its own treatment by operation.
And moreover, there are abscesses which should not be punctured until maturity of the skin in those or completion of them.
Some abscesses must be opened when they are crossed, and not mature according to their completion, such as abscesses that are near joints, for an abscess when it is near a joint its being is prolonged until one puts pressure on what is in the circuit of it, and often its ligaments or nerves are corrupted by it, causing contraction of that limb; or it is an abscess near a main limb, and if you delay opening it until it is matured, it will harm the main limb; or it is near the buttocks, therefore open it immature so that you do not tear the skin of it nor elongate it to the parts inside the buttocks, and make a fistula or one which cannot be healed in its term. But you should know the time of opening an abscess, and that is when it is matured.
And know that it is mature when there is relaxation of pain and cessation of fever, and before the decrease of heat and pulsation, and sharpness of the head of the abscess, and other signs.
And know that you should open it where there is more pus, near the abscess, and where pus comes from curing the elevation.
And opening is always done along the length of the flesh or body if abscesses are in the parts of the breast or thighs and the joints, ligaments, nerves, arteries; and finally in all other places where reflection does not occur.
But when the abscess is in a fleshy place, it is better to leave opening it until digestion of it is confirmed according to its completion, as we have said; for if you open it beforehand, the body of the pus will be prolonged and much dirt will accumulate, and often the lips of it will become hardened and the depth of it.
But some abscesses are opened across the width of the flesh or body according to necessity, or according to what that limb needs.
And you should make small openings, and in large abscesses make a large opening or many incisions according to the diversity of their size.
And there are some abscesses in which the chain should be curved and cut when it is done thus as with bread, and when it is done it sticks until it is healed, such as those that occur in swellings of the glands and buboes.
And among those are ones that are incised with three angles; and among them are ones which are incised like the figure of a mitre leaf, such as those of hernias.
And among them are those in which round incision and crescentic incision are administered, resembling these.
But that one to which it is not suited like those abscesses on the surface should be opened with a superficial opening or flat one only.
And when the abscess is large and has collected much pus, you should open it but do not try to remove all the pus at that time; having removed some of it, pack the abscess again the next day and gradually remove more each time until it is completely drained.
And especially if the patient is a child with vertigo, or a pregnant woman, or a small infant, or an elderly person in decrepitude, because often the vital spirit is weakened by the exit of pus and death occurs. Therefore be cautious!
Therefore be careful with this chapter and also the opening you make when opening these abscesses. Be sure to cleanse the edges of the wound and consider whether the edge of the abscess is small or has a flat section, then apply the appropriate dressing according to that. If the abscess is large and the incisions are many, then pause between each pull until they drain together.
"When an abscess bursts, releasing part of the chain or having its concavity opened in the area, then you should fill it with lint thread or cloth thread, just as when you pull out bread loaves or roots, without moisture; and strengthen that on the third day; and then proceed and treat it until it heals."
"If blood flow occurs during the operation, then you should administer water and vinegar mixed on a cloth of linen, and place it on the location of the bleeding several times."
"If the bleeding persists, then you should administer treatment and care, and powders that have been recommended in many places of this book and division."
"But if it is wintertime, and the location of the abscess is a place with many nerves, then you should mix powders in hot vinegar and oil, and place them on those locations."
"And if it is summertime, and the locations are fleshy, then you should place powders mixed with water and oil or vinegar and oil, and all of that should be done within three days, as we have said, and then you should release the abscess and cleanse it, and administer to its care whatever is appropriate until it heals."
"And this is what is necessary regarding the knowledge of the treatment of abscesses generally, but according to the way of distinction, I have already spoken about each abscess in particular manner through chapters singularly."
"Chapter XLII."
"Of Incision of Abscesses that occur on the Neck."
"On the neck of the child, there are small abscesses and types of knots that contain tunics which are made from them; and the types of them are many."
"And among them are pimples, and those that contain moisture similar to lime." "And among them are those that contain moisture similar to powder, and they resemble each other; and among them are those that are rocky and hard."
"And in the section of all of them, and in their extraction, there is no fear, for their extraction does not cause any pain."
"And the operation in sectioning them is that you spread them apart with an instrument whose shape is shown approximately here, which is called 'entromes,' until you know what they contain."
"But if what it contains is moisture, then you should cut it open with a section along its length through a superficial section according to this form:"
"And begin the section at line B to line G. Then, when the moisture is evacuated, you should scrape that out which contains that moisture, and do not leave any cause of it, for otherwise viewed abscesses return if something remains."
"And then immerse it in Egyptian pitch, if available, and otherwise in water and salt; and fill it with that and leave it until the next day, for with this you will corrode all that remains of that skin."
"And then iterate over that wound with Egyptian pitch a second and third time if necessary until you are confident that there is no remaining cause of that skin; then dress the wound with ointment until it heals."
"And if an abscess contains fatty knots, then you should incise it according to this form:" "with a section having the shape of a cross, and make an incision between both lips of the section and scrape it all out, and use your strength in extracting the tunic which contains it."
"But if there is any pain to you, then do what I told you first."
"And similarly do with the stony abscess in sectioning and treating it according to what we have said; for sectioning a stony abscess is easier because it contains little blood and moisture."
"And sometimes there are some of these abscesses which are in the head in some men with whom there is no moisture at all; and this cause is that once someone incised an abscess on the head of an old woman and found it to be like a deaf stone, rough and white, which could not be broken open. And if anyone were struck by that, he would have been injured."
"But in other accidental abscesses in the head except for this one, it is not like that. Thus, the section of these all should be a superficial section."
"And pause the perforation of those whose bottom part is low because it may alleviate the body from the lower parts."
"And then treat them with whatever is appropriate for their treatment."
"Chapter XLII."
"On the section of scrofula that occurs in the neck."
"Many times these abscesses occur in the collar, in the armpits, and in the groins; and sometimes they occur in other parts of the body."

"And the species of these scrofula are many because among them there are some stony ones, and some contain moisture, and some are malignant which do not obey treatment."
"Therefore in that one which you find to be of good disposition in the touch, whose color is close to the color of bone, and is soft all over, not annexed to the nerve of the neck or the veins or the artery, and not prominent, it is necessary for you to incise it with a superficial section from above to below on the body from line G to line B. Then scrape it out entirely, and extend the lips of the bone with forceps, or with several forceps if you need them, as we have said in the abscesses of the head, and extract it little by little."
"And be especially careful not to incise any veins or nerves."
"And do not use a sharp spatula, for it may cause your hand to slip during the incision or worsen the disease. And do not incise anything that does not need to be incised; because if you were to incise a vein or an artery and hinder yourself from your operation, then pause with a vetriol plaster or other powders which stop bleeding, and apply it, and leave it until the sharpness of the abscess has paused and the wound has softened and begins to heal." "So return to your operation once it is completed."

Capítulo XLIII
Of the incision of the point of an accidental aposteme within the scrotum.
It was said by the ancients that this section is made in the epiglottis; yet we have not seen anyone in our land who has done it.
And this is the inscription of the sermon of those people
But in men who have a squinting eye, it is advisable to avoid the extraction of the epiglottis since by this there is not made any improvement and all the veins and the major blood vessels are here.
But in those who have apostemes cauterized in the mouth or scrotum or ears, when the illness is not on the skin, it is advisable to avoid section of the epiglottis to escape the damage that is done by perforation.
Therefore when we want this, we should incise the epiglottis at three circles of the rings of the epiglottis, or four with a small section across its width in that which is between two rings by quantity, so that the incision is made in cartilage and not in the cartilage itself; and this place is convenient for section because it is devoid of flesh and the vessels of blood are far from it.
And if the doctor is fearful, he should beforehand extend the cord of the scrotum with a hook, and carefully cut the cord within until it reaches the canal, but avoid the vessels of blood if any are visible.
And then incise the cartilage as we have recommended; and it is indicated by the swelling above the section of the canal, which is of that fluid and of what comes out from its disruption and by the absence of voice.
Leave the wound open for some time.
Therefore when the hour has passed in which perforation is feared, approximate two lips of the edge of the wound and leave that alone be the cartilage.
And then apply medicines that cause flesh to grow within so that it may heal.
"Albucasis said that the summary of our discourse is this: Some of these ulcers have already closed the throat of the patient, and the patient has come into death; the breath of the patient has been cut off, and some go to incise the epiglottis so that the patient may breathe on the place of the ulcer by some respiration, and thus be saved from death."
"You should thus let the ulcer heal inside until the evil of the illness is consumed. The evil lasts for three days. Then you should dress it thus, and care for it until it heals."
"I saw that a servant took a knife and put it in her throat and cut out a part of the lung's bronchus. I was called to cure her, and I found her moaning like one dead. I uncovered the ulcer and drew out the blood which was flowing from the ulcer."
"Therefore I was forced to confess that she had not cut any vein nor artery, and the wind issued from the ulcer. And I cured her thus until she was healed."
"And it did not happen to the servant that any air came out of her throat. And after some days she returned to her usual state of health."
"Now you say that there is no danger in cutting into the epiglottis."
Chapter 44.
Of an incision for an aposteme that happens outside of the throat, which is called a thyregocele (thyroid goitre).
This aposteme named thyroid goiter is a large aposteme according to the color of the body, and it is common in women.
And it happens in two ways: either naturally or accidentally.
"It is not Nature's way to heal."
"And accidents occur in two ways: the first is similar to solid tumors, and the second is similar to an abscess that occurs due to the rupture of an artery; this one is dangerous." Chapter XLVI
"On the section of the various types of tumors."
Of the many species of joints, I have already mentioned all their kinds in the division.
And since you ask thus for the difference between joint and outlet with doubt
Therefore you say that in outlet there is heat and fever and violent pain within when the boiling of the excess fluid stops; and it is full putrefaction which then ceases the fever, the pain, and the heat.
But in joint there is neither heat nor fever nor pain, and it contains that thick fluid which is in the proper bladder.
And it is according to the color of the body, and its beginning is like a haze and it becomes thus like emptiness, whether greater or lesser, and there are two species, for some are thick and contain moisture, and the colors of the moisture are many, as you said in the division.
Therefore, when you reach the cure of joint, that you remove it and investigate it at its beginning with an instrument which is called "intromes," according to what its form will come in the chapter which is appropriate for this.
And it is the manner of investigation of boils and of all joints, and it is that you take this instrument and insert it into the most humid place which you find in the boil, and you turn your fingers with that little by little until you know that the instrument has pierced the skin.
And then lastly, according to the measure of the size of the boil, extract the intromes and consider what is issued in the tract of it.
And if running moisture has been forgotten, whatever its color may be, then you should incise it with a superficial section according to what I have said in the case of other boils.
And if from the tract of the intromes there is no moisture, then know that it is thick (grassa).
If it is dry above it with a section having the form of a cross in this manner: Thus as you have shown, suspend that with hooks and tear out the chain from all parts with ease, and guard the skin or bag, if possible, over it and draw out that fluid.
But if it breaks during the operation, it is not possible to draw out that fluid. Many times there remains some inside and then you draw it out piece by piece without any cause for concern.
For if there remains any cause, little or much, the knot will return according to its nature.
And if some small part remains, then fill the wound with some sharp corrosive powders and strengthen it, and press on that which seems to be an abscess, and cure it with the other treatment until it is healed.
And if the knot is large, then cut both lips of it and heal it with that which enters into it.
But if there is no pulsating vein on it, or not pulsating, then cut and cauterize the place where it was with three-forked cautery that is vitriol, and leave that open for two or three days until the wound closes and the ebullition of blood returns; and again return to excising what remains of the knot.

"Regarding the cutting of boils that occur by force or through a vein."
"When the artery is broken and the vein above it is constricted, many times a boil occurs. "Chapter LI
"Chapter on the treatment of prominence of the navel."
"Prominence of the navel occurs due to many causes: either from fissures in the skin above the belly, or from tissue or bowel protruding through other ruptures; or from blood flowing from a vein or artery, as mentioned before; or from obstructed wind in it."
"But if it is due to a fissure in the skin and protrusion of tissue, then the boil will have a similar color to that of the skin; it will be painless and appear in various locations." "But if it is due to protrusion of bowel, then the location of that boil will be as we have described earlier, with great variation and diversity. And when you press it with your fingers, it disappears but quickly returns. And there will be much pain and difficulty with washing and effort."
"But if it is due to moisture, then it will be painless and not disappear when pressed by your hand. It will not become hard or enlarged."
"And if it is due to blood, then the boil will appear with these signs becoming dark in color."
"But if it is due to prolapsed flesh, then it will be a severe boil that is large and hard, depending on the quantity of tissue protruding."
"But if it is due to wind, then touching it will cause no pain."
"First, examine whether the navel's prominence is due to blood vessel or vein swelling, or windiness. If so, refrain from treating him, for in that case there is fear and dread, as taught in the chapter where it says 'abscesses by blood vessel and vein.'"
"If the navel's prominence is due to bowel or tissue, you should then have the patient hold their breath while standing upright and extended. Next, examine all around the umbilical area with your finger, then command them to bend forward between their thighs over their two knees; then circumscribe the umbilical area with a broad spatula where your finger has indicated. Then extend the swelling of the abscess upwards using forceps, and finally ligate it firmly but gently in a proper manner."
"Then cut through the middle of the extended abscess down to the ligament and insert your finger into that opening while seeking the bowel. If you find it and keep it firm with your fingers, then carefully extract it and push it back inside the abdomen."
"And if you have found tissue instead of bowel, then grasp it with forceps, and cut away its excesses."
"But if it is a vein or artery that you encounter, then encircle it with a ligature and return to your operation. Take two needles, tie strong thread onto them, insert the needles into the previously made incision around the abscess in such a way as to form a cross, penetrate them; then pull the abscess in four directions over the needles."
"And if you wish, remove the needles and allow the skin to heal by itself. Or else cut away the excess when it has healed over, and then care for it with water until it is completely healed."
"And if the prominence of the navel is due to fat or moisture, then you should cut away the abscess as we have described and drain out any blood or moisture that you find there. Then treat it with water and ensure that the area is healed."
Chapter Liii
"On treating a carbuncle."
"We have already spoken, in the division on the type of carbuncle and how it is treated with medicines, that using iron to treat it should be avoided as it can cause ulceration. We have also mentioned that a carbuncle can occur due to improper care during treatment."
"And the ancients said that sometimes carbuncles can occur in places where it is possible to eradicate them completely, such as those on the breasts or buttocks, and especially when they are small at the beginning."
"But when it is advanced and large, do not attempt to treat it yourself, for you will not be able to heal such an ulcer nor have I seen another case, nor has it been recorded."
"And the operation for treating it is when it is located as we have described, which is to first let the inflammation subside and purge with black hellebore several times, then incise it if there is a noticeable swelling."
"And then prepare the inflammation with a preparation suitable for the location of the operation. Then excise the base of the carbuncle using forceps that are suitable for it, and scrape away all the surrounding tissue with great care to ensure that there is no remaining cause of the infection." "And let the blood flow freely, do not remove it too hastily, express the area, and absorb all the thick blood with your hand or an instrument that is at your disposal."
"But if you find it difficult to deal with the thick blood, then make an incision into a vein or artery nearby in order to reduce the flow of blood. Then cauterize that area until the bleeding stops, and treat it with the other methods until it is healed."
Chapter Liv
"On the treatment of dropsy."
"We have already described, in the division (of diseases), the species of dropsy due to water and their signs, and their treatment with medicines."
"And that which is cured with iron is only the species of ascites alone, and it is not approached with iron to the species of tympany nor to the species of hydrops archi, for this is mortal."
"And when you have treated this species of tympanitic dropsy with medicines and it does not improve, then consider whether the patient has already attained debility, or if there is another dropsy present, as in cases of coughing or abdominal distention and similar ones. Then be careful not to treat them with iron, for there is fear concerning this."
"But if the disease is one of excess of natural heat, and there is no other disease present but dropsy alone, not infancy or old age, then the method of operation is as follows: you should elevate the patient between your thighs, and the assistant should press the abdomen with his hand, expressing water from it near the navel, and then take a sharp-pointed spatula in this manner:"
"It should be double-pointed and long, with a sharp extremity like a spatula; but nevertheless it should have some shortness little by little, so that in the operation you do not pass into the bowels, and thus harm him."
"And then consider if the dropsy is due to an obstruction of the bowels, for in that case you should make your incision at a distance from the navel by three fingerbreadths on the right side above the pubic hair."
"But if the dropsy is due to a disease of the liver, then your incision should be on the left side of the navel by three fingerbreadths."
"And if the cause of the dropsy is the spleen, then your incision should be on the left side."
"Make sure your section (operation) is on the side where you want to place the patient, so that excess fluids do not flow to that area."
"Then carefully pierce with the instrument all along the canal, and when you reach that section, raise your hand with the spoon between the canal and the spermatic cord, and remove that; if the amount is about the size of a nail or less."
"And then pierce the spermatic cord until you reach the desired location, which is where water flows in." "Then remove that and insert an instrument with the following shape:" "And it resembles a thin silver cannula; it is made of silver or iron or laton lion, at the lower part of which there is a small hole, and on its sides there are three holes: two on one side and one on the other side; and its tip is cut obliquely like a pen feather."
"And at the upper end of it there is a ring, because when the instrument reaches the water, that moment it begins to suck on the instrument, hence it evacuates water in equal quantity at the same time; for if you evacuate more than necessary at that moment, it will quickly cause death by resolving its animal spirit, or approach death."
"But evacuate according to the quantity of the virtue of the instrument, and according to what you understand about the conditions of the illness, the virtue of its pulse, and its quality."
"And then remove the instrument, and retain the water that is held by the spermatic cord which holds the hole through which you pierced it according to this manner."
"And then repeat the operation on another day if the illness tolerates it, and remove a small quantity of water, and do this for several days with fear that you should not leave too much water."
"But if you are afraid of the illness and leave too much water, then treat it with a grave sepulture in dry sand, and much sweat in baths, and expose it to sunlight for a long time; and treat it with drying medicines until it is healed."
"And cauterize the stomach, and the mesentery near the extraction of the water, according to what I have described previously."
"Chapter 50."

"And beware in your operation for flux of blood, because many times this occurs; and pause with this that you cut the blood vessels, and cure the wound until it is healed."

"Chapter LVI."
"Of the purification of infants and of the cure for what happens to them at circumcision."
Circumcision is not a solution for continuity like other diseases: but since it is our operation and within our control, especially in children, we must assign the best operation and path to preserve health more easily.
Therefore it is said that the ancients did not mention circumcision in all of their books because they did not use it in their laws. However, since we have acquired this practice through experience, I have found that most artisans and barbers use circumcision with a knife and clamps; and they use lime plaster and nail scissors for the incision.
And I have already tested all these methods and did not find better circumcision with forceps, lime plaster that uses the nail scissors for incision. For many times it escapes the frenulum upwards, because the frenulum of the foreskin has two layers, and the inner layer remains below; and it is very easy to cause another incision and certain pain. Chapter LXII
Of Incision for Inguinal Hernia
Inguinal hernia is nothing but an aggregation of moisture in the white membrane which lies outside the spermatic cord containing the testicle, and it is called a processus vaginalis.
And sometimes it is in the proper parietal wall which nature has prepared for the reception of the testicle, but it is already another testicle; and it is the spermatic cord between the white membrane which we have mentioned, and it is nothing but fat.
The cause of this hernia is weakness that occurs in the testicles, so that through them this matter escapes and sometimes it happens due to a violent blow on the testicles.
This moisture has many colors, for its color is declining to yellow or sanguineous red, or brown, or it is blackish-white, or clear watery-white, and this is what is most common.
And the signs by which it is known where this aggregation of water is located are these: for if it is in the white membrane that we have mentioned, then the swelling will be round and slightly elongated like a figure of an egg, and the testicle appears because the moisture contains it on all sides.
And if the moisture is in the proper parietal wall, then the swelling will be round with a depression of the testicle and because of this one might estimate that it is another testicle.
And if the moisture is between the spermatic cord and the white membrane, then the contents will be felt separately.
And when you want to know the color of the moisture, then press on the swelling with an instrument whose shape is appropriate for this purpose. And according to what comes out in the trace of the instrument, judge what is inside it.
Therefore, when we come to the treatment of it with iron, then it is necessary that we command the patient to be flaccid if possible, and empty his body.
And then let him lie on his back slightly higher than his head and put many cloths under him.
And then sit on the left side of him and command the minister to be at his right side. Let him extend his arm two palms wide at the spermatic cord and the opening of the abdominal wall.
And then take a broad-bladed knife and incise the spermatic cord in the middle as far as possible towards the penis.
And let the incision be made according to the rule with equal distance from the line that should divide the skin of the testicles until it reaches the white membrane containing.
And strip that, observe it, and guard yourself for this so that you do not incise it. And your stripping with which you strip it should be done gently so that it is suspended with the testicle more finely and carefully explore it according to its quantity as much as possible.
And then perforate the water-filled membrane with a broad perforation, and remove all the water.
And then separate between two lips of the incision with forceps and extend the membrane at its sides. Do not touch the spermatic cord containing the testicle, and incise the membrane in that manner which is possible for you. Incise that completely or in pieces and especially its finer sides, for if you do not carefully scrutinize the incision of it, it is not certain that the water will not return.
But if the testicle appears outside its cord during your operation, then when you have completed the incision of the membrane, return it inside that and then join together the two lips of the spermatic cord with suturing. And then dress it like other wounds until it is healed.
And if you find the testicle corrupted by another disease, then it is necessary that you ligate its vessels which are on top of the suspender and remove it. And then dress it with what we have said.
But if water accumulates in two places at the same time, know that there are two hernias. Therefore, incise that part according to what you have done in the other one equally. And if it appears to be an operation, then perform it.
"And then you shall clean the blood, and insert into the sections wool immersed in oil or rosemary-infused oil; and place over another wool which you have immersed in wine and oil, and spread it over both knees and the navel of the belly; and place over folded cloths and powders, and bind those over with linen, which is prepared thus:"

Chapter LXV.
"Regarding the treatment of intestinal hernia."
"The occurrence of this hernia is due to a separation in the diaphragm that extends over the abdomen on both sides of the naval, allowing some loops of intestine from that rupture to descend into it."

"If the time is prolonged by this [the colic], an appropriate incision must be made into the colon where the intestine enters it; and this occurs because of the dilation of the colon which is in the groin area as we have said, the cause being that the colon has extended, and nearby areas become softened and the location becomes inflamed and swollen."
"And its treatment is by cautery, as described above."
"And sometimes it is treated with iron according to this manner: the sick person lies on their back between two blankets, and then the location of the swollen and inflamed carbuncles is dried by a lateral section made according to their size."
"And then strengthen the white colon that is below the backbone so that it is uncovered."
And then take the wand and place it on the prominent part of the hip, and press it firmly against the front of the abdomen.
And then choose two prominent points on the end of the wand placed over the hip bone and adjust them close to each other with one next to the other.
And then extract the end of the wand, ensuring that none of the intestines remain inside the inguinal canal, neither stretched out nor otherwise distorted, as you should know from your knowledge of intestinal hernia treatment.
And then cure it with the treatment for hernias, and after opening the skin, cleanse it and restore the hernia until it is consolidated; because the inguinal canal contracts and does not adjust to the prominence of rupture.
And cautery is better at this location, as it is closer to safety.
Capitolum lxviii.
On the Softening of the Spermatic Cord
Many times, the spermatic cord in some men is softened due to this fact that the tissues between it are softened, and it is noticeable to observe it.
Therefore, it is necessary for someone who is treated for this to make the patient lie down according to his condition, and cut all of the softened spermatic cord over the natural one; then approximate the lips with a suture.
And if you wish, at the beginning cut off the excess of the softened spermatic cord with three or four stitches and firmly suture it.
And then incise between the sutures; and then treat with treatment for other hernias until it is healed, and the testicles fall back into place.
Capitolum lxix.
On Castration
Know that castration is condemned in our law, but for the sake of learning I remember it here in this book; and it is not necessary to remember it except for two methods, one of which is so that it may be within the knowledge of the physician when he is questioned about it, so that he knows how to treat it if it occurs; and the other method is because we often have need of castration of other beasts for our purposes, such as with many horses, and oxen, and pigs, and similar animals.
And therefore I say that castration is done in two ways: either by crushing or by cutting with an incision.
"When injury occurs from a fall, the procedure is to first plunge the beast into boiling water until its joints are softened and then let them hang." "And then take those with your hand carefully, so they do not slip away from the touch."
"When castration is done through incision and section, you should hold the beast and press its testicular cord with your left hand."
"And then ligate the suspensory ligament, and make an incision on each side between two testicles."
"Then cut those that you want to remove." "And do not leave any of the skin around it [the testicle], but peel off the skin carefully which is on top of the vessels."
"And this method of castration is better when done by crushing, because strong crushing leaves no trace of the testicles so that the beast desires copulation."
"And then treat the wound until it heals."
Chapter LXX.
"On Hermaphrodism."
"Hermaphrodism in males occurs in two ways: one is when it appears as something like a sheath in the space between the testicular cord, and that which is between two testicles resembles a female vulva with skin around its opening."
"And sometimes urine comes out of that which is on the cord of the testicles."
"But in females, it is one species: namely that the vulva of the female over the pubis appears like two male testicles, somewhat resembling the opening of the foreskin as with the male penis and two testicles."
"And its treatment is of three kinds: two in males and one kind in females." "And it is necessary to cut away that flesh attached so that the emission of that which escapes may be stopped, and then treat it with the cure for other wounds."
"And in the second kind in males where urine flows from the cord of the testicles, there is neither cure nor operation in it."
Chapter XXI.
"On Lentigo and Raised Flesh Caused by Women."
"Freckles are naturally attached and appear in the skin of those who have been rubbed, and are made worse by carelessness; some women have them greatly increased so that they spread like those in men, even to copulation."
"Then you should remove the excess of freckles with your hand or with an ointment and scrape them off."
"And do not end in incision, especially on the forehead, lest there be a flow of blood."
"And then treat it with the cure for wounds until it is healed."
"But raised flesh is flesh that grows in the horror of the mother's womb until it fills that space, and it often appears at the opening of the foreskin like a tail (and for this reason some people first called it "tail sickness"); therefore we should scrape it away just as we do with freckles, and treat it until it is healed."
Chapter LXXII.
"On the Cure of Herpes Zoster."
"Herpes zoster is when the vulva of the female is not pierced, or has a small opening." "And it is either natural or accidental."
"Accidental ones are due to previous illness, and they are made up of flesh that has grown too much, or from skin tags, or from thick or thin membranes."
"And they are found either on the forehead of the mother, or on her ribs, or on her belly above or below, and they prevent copulation and pregnancy and childbirth, and often prevent menstruation."
"And its recognition is made by the careful examination of the vulva, if the opening is obvious; but if it is not obvious, you should examine it with your fingers or with a speculum."
"But if the opening is due to a thin membrane, and it is between the two labia, then cut it and tear it apart."
"And if it appears over both of the labia majora, then put your fingers on both sides of them as shown above."
"And the woman should be on her back with her thighs spread apart, and then spread both labia with force so that this thin membrane is broken and the opening is made wider."
"And then take wool dipped in oil and place it on that spot, and leave it there for a day so that the wound does not become stuck together."
"But if the membrane is thick and coarse, then you should cut it with a broad blade or with myrtle leaves."
"But if the opening is due to flesh that has grown too much, then suspend it with an ointment and scrape it away."
"And use the medicines that stop bleeding without being bitten, such as aloe, dragon's blood, and frankincense mixed with album graecum."
"And then administer a wide leaden cannula to prevent the wound from healing too quickly."
"And keep it like that for several days and apply hot water compresses."
"And then treat it with the other cure for consolidation until it is healed."
"And sometimes it happens that other fleshes are born from the mother's birth canal, and then you should cut them according to this method." "But if it is due to a hard abscess, then do not use iron in any way on the hard abscess that is in the mother's birth canal."
Chapter LXXIII.
"On the treatment of hemorrhoids, tailbone pain, and redness that occurs in the area around women's genitals."
"Hemorrhoids are caused by many veins that continuously receive too much blood, and when they become old and stretched out, they create pain."
"I have already mentioned the types of hemorrhoids and their characteristics earlier, and I will now say which ones require treatment and which ones do not."
"Therefore, I say that hemorrhoids and piles that are in the front of the anus but do not protrude and cannot be felt do not require treatment with iron."
"However, those that are at the opening of the anus and can be felt are the ones that need to be treated."
"It is necessary that you insert the woman's finger into her anus and gently extend it with forceps or rough cloth, and incise those with scissors."
"And gently sprinkle powder made from the flowers of the oak tree or similar on those wounds to stop the bleeding."
"And then have her sit quietly for an hour, and afterwards apply hot water compresses."
"And if the bleeding persists, then make her drink a decoction of sumac, oak bark, pomegranate rind, and similar."
"And also take barley flour mixed with honey, vinegar, and warm water and make a poultice to apply on the area."
"And if the bleeding is stopped, that's good. But if not, then attach two cupping glasses and perform scarification on the breasts."
"And also take wool and soak it in juice of coriander or juice of rue or juice of wall germander with white wine, then apply it to the area and cover it with a warm cloth until healed."
"And heal it until it is healed."
Chapter LXXIV
About accidental perforation of the bladder during childbirth.
Many kinds of apostumes can happen accidentally in childbirth, such as hard tumors and stone-like apostumes and ulcers and adhesions and hernias and fistulas and hemorrhages and tears and other apostumes. "And I have already spoken about these illnesses and their types and symptoms and treatments in the division."
"But I must explain in this treatise how to cauterize an apostume that appears in the bladder when it is of those that heal, and if you want to know how the operation is done with iron."
"Therefore, you should consider whether the pain of the apostume at its beginning is acute with percussion and chills and fever, and if it tends to swell and if pressure on it causes discomfort, then do not cut into it, and treat it with something that promotes maturation until the sharpness of the accident ceases."
"But then you should make the woman lie on her back on a pillow that has two pillows; and recline her on her back and adjust her feet so they are higher than her hips, and let her thighs be spread apart, and pause her arms by her sides, and tie each one with a suitable ligature."
"And then the midwife should stand on the right side and administer the instrument with which the opening of the bladder is widened, the shape of which will be described in the relevant cases."
"And when you want to administer this instrument, you should stand at the entrance of the woman's vagina and make sure that only the tip of the instrument enters the bladder and not more than what is necessary for the illness." "But if the instrument is larger than the opening of the bladder, then you should place pledgets on the tissue around the opening of the bladder to prevent any instrument from entering it."
"And you should place the tip of a probe on the left side above and make sure that the person administering the instrument holds it and rotates the tip until the opening of the bladder is widened."
"And when the excretion appears and it is touched with the hand and it is clear and thin, then you should dry it with a linen cloth using the tip of the spatula."
"And when the healing is evacuated, then you should place in the wound a wick soaked in rose oil or green oil in which there is some astringency and place it at the section of the opening of the bladder."
"And then cover the bladder and put clean wool moistened with water in which mallows have been boiled on top."
"And after two days, it should be dressed again with an ointment that is suitable for promoting maturation until it is healed."
"And sometimes the bladder and the wound are washed in such a way that they are christened with water and honey, and sometimes with water in which red rose leaves or long-stalked aristolochia have been boiled, and then the ointment is reapplied."
"If the wound becomes inflamed inside the bladder, then you should be prohibited from cauterizing it with iron, but rather treat it with what we have said in the division."
"Chapter 75"
"To teach midwives how to treat twisted births that are not in a natural position."
"It is necessary for the midwife to know at the beginning the signs of a natural birth so that when she sees the woman pushing at the entrance and desiring to smell the air, and upon that she is relieved by what is above her from the birth, and hastens the exit of the child, then she knows that this birth is in a natural position, and the second one comes out on its back with its face down or suspended or hanging by the umbilical cord."
"So when you see these signs, then the belly of the child should be compressed so that the embryo comes out gently when it is on its back, and then the second one comes out on its back with its face down or suspended or hanging by the umbilical cord, and it should be cleansed of those superfluities with good cleansing."
"But any other position of this birth is unnatural and undesirable because when the child comes out on its feet with its body coming out in front of its head with its feet facing downward, or one hand or a foot comes out first, or it comes out head down with one arm, or its abdomen comes out first, then it turns its face upwards, and these are the figures of an unnatural birth."
"Therefore it is necessary for the midwife to be wise and subtle in all those cases and to guard against errors and deception."
"And here I will show all of these figures and what position is indicated by each one and how it should be corrected."

"But when it is extracted inside the thighs, then you should tell him to cough and make him sneeze with caution, because if God wills, he may soon forget."
"And if it is not forgotten with what we have mentioned, then you should gradually return the fetus inside until it falls down according to its natural figure, because it will soon be forgotten with a gentle extraction."

The lateral extraction of the baby while keeping one of your hands in place. If the head does not reduce easily with your hand, then raise the woman's buttocks and help that part come out.
If it still cannot come out, then have her lie down on the bed, strike the baby's buttocks forcefully with your fist, and then administer warm liquids or remedies made from mucilaginous plants.
If the child has been born, then have the mother lie down on her back, and carefully examine the reduction of the hand. Then wrap the baby according to its natural shape, make the woman sneeze, and tell her to push until it is completely out.
Extraction of the baby with both hands by grasping the shoulders and turning them towards the mother's back. The midwife should hold the baby's head with one hand and gently turn it little by little, helping it to come out more easily.
When the head is out and as much of the baby's body has been born as possible, then pause briefly to apply the oil and mucilage mixture that we have recommended.
Then command her to push gently little by little. When you have done this, then have her lie down on one hip and tell her to lean over towards the right side, and command her to bear down; make her sneeze conditionally. Preparation for the exit of the fetus onto its side.

If the baby is suspended by its face and neck, then insert your finger into the amniotic sac to release it and prevent suffocation.
Then gently push the baby out through the birth canal as necessary, pausing when it is appropriate to do so. Command the woman to bear down several times, and with God's help, the baby will be born easily.
The exit of twins or multiple fetuses. Know that many twins are born, and sometimes three or four, but this is rare and unusual. There are several causes for this, but it is not something that occurs frequently in life.
If there are multiple fetuses or twins joined together by their membranes, then separate them carefully. Each one has its own umbilical cord and amniotic sac. Sometimes they can be born naturally like any other baby, but sometimes they may need assistance in being born, as we have discussed.
If some of them are difficult to deliver and come to what we have said about unnatural positions, then care for them as we have discussed.
And if the midwife is skilled and does what she does with ease and skillfulness, and with patience, and acts according to her knowledge as prepared by God for bringing about health.
Memorandum: What forms in the womb from embryos and aborts
Sometimes there are formed in the womb one, two, three, four, five, six, seven, and even more than ten fetuses. It has been verified that a woman aborted six at once, and another bore ten all at once. The cause of this was due to measurement by learned physicians.
And it is important that the midwife knows how to deal with this situation well, and therefore she should pause if necessary according to what is appropriate.
Chapter 76
Of delivering a dead baby
When you are caring for a dead baby as we have discussed in the division on treatment and it has not yet been born, and you wish to use an operation with your hand, then you should consider whether the woman is of good health and does not have any of the conditions that could cause harm.
Then it is necessary for the woman to be placed on her left side with her head lowered and her hips elevated.
And the assistant should hold the woman from both sides or lie next to her on the bed, so that her body does not extend during the extraction of the baby.
Then you should moisten the mouth of the womb with olive oil mixed with mucilage of marsh mallow and fenugreek seeds.
And then the midwife should anoint her hand with those oils and mucilages, and gently insert it into the womb. Then she should search for where the fingers can grasp the baby's ankles
The suitable places to grasp the baby are: therefore, consider if the baby is positioned head down. If so, grasp its heels or neck or mouth or palate or beard or wishbone or near the ribs or hypochondria.
But if the baby is positioned feet down, then grasp it by the penis or the middle of its back
It is necessary to grasp the baby with your right hand and pause its curvature in that spot between your left fingers. Then gently insert your left hand and place your fingers on one of those locations we have mentioned until you reach the baby's body.
Then pause and grasp with another finger or the third if necessary, so that there is equal traction and not just pulling along its natural curvature.
It should be done gently in every delivery, so that the baby's emergence is eased just as it happens when removing a tooth.
And it is important that the extraction be done gently between them. If any part of the baby becomes stuck, then the midwife should anoint her fingers with oil and carefully insert them and twist those parts that are stuck
Therefore, if the delivery of the baby is difficult, then change your grasp to another place that may be easier. Do this until the entire baby has been delivered.
But if one hand is extended before the other and it is not possible to reduce that by its curvature, then a cloth should be wrapped around it. Then extract that until everything has been delivered, and cut it either at the junction of the fingers or at the joint.
And do the same with the other hand and both feet
But if the baby's head is large or its curvature becomes injured during delivery, or there is water in the fontanelle, then insert a pair of forceps between the fingers and tear the skin to facilitate extraction of the fluid or use an instrument called "alundat" whose shape will be shown with the other instruments in the next chapter.
Similarly, if the baby has a large head by nature, then cut it with scissors or use an "alundat" as mentioned earlier to facilitate extraction of the bones using forceps
If the head has exited and is compressed beneath the collarbone, then it should be cut so that the humidity in the chest may escape.
If it is not complicated or difficult, without making any incisions, then you should cut the head as soon as you can.
If the patient's abdomen is inflamed or they are suffering from dropsy, then it is necessary for you to pierce there so that the fluid may flow out.
But if the fetus is lying on its back, then its attraction will be light and its direction towards the mouth of the womb will be easy.
But if it is compressed beneath the abdomen and the chest, then you should remove it with cloth that you will have wrapped around your hand, and cut the abdomen and chest so that water may flow out of them.
But if the other limbs are out and the head is turned back, then insert your left hand; but if the mouth of the womb is covered, then insert your hand into the uterus, encircle the head with it, pull it down towards the mouth of the womb, and then insert a hook or two hooks and pull it down with them.
And if the mouth of the womb is obstructed by an ulcerous inflammation that has occurred in it, then you should not be careless about this. In such cases, it may be necessary to administer an evacuation for excess fatty humidities. And apply poultices; and follow the patient with moistening and softening waters.
And if the fetus is lying on its side, then if it is possible, turn it: and administer what has been said for a live fetus.
And if that is not possible, then cut through the ribs and extract it.
You should not leave any cause inside the secondine.
And when you have completed all of your operation, then administer what has been said about the cure for ulcerous inflammations that occur in the womb.
And if bleeding occurs, then apply astringent waters and administer the other treatment.
"I have seen a woman whose belly was killed dead, and shortly afterwards she became pregnant again, but the child died as well." "An abscess happened to him in his belly quite some time ago; it swelled up there where the wound opened, and then he began to suffer."
"And I was called to care for him and treated him for a long time, but his illness did not improve."
I place upon him certain poultices with great attraction, and I remove from him one bone, and afterward it passes some days, and I remove another bone; but I was greatly amazed, because there are no bones in the belly.
And then I thought that they were of the dead man's bones.
Therefore I treated the plague, and extracted from him many bones, the woman who was in her best condition, and she lived thus for a long time, running from him with only one small arm.
And I did not think it was strange, for in this there is science and help for what the skilled physician effects with his hand to administer cure.

Shape of vessel with which the mother is opened:

"Regarding the extraction of the placenta."
