"Treatment for fistulas that come from there."
"The fistulas that begin in the lower part of the buttocks are usually hard and large, which begin near the anus outside or in the space between the thighs."
"And it is one fistula or more."
"And since that hard swelling is old and runs with humid pus or thin purulent matter, sometimes there are some penetrating fistulas."
"And those penetrating fistulas are known by what flows from them through the exit and by the windiness; and sometimes there is a feeling of discharge, and it often comes out as worms."
"And sometimes from those fistulas there are penetrating fistulas into the bladder and into the urethra, and into the junction of the vagina and into the rectum."
"And how a penetrating fistula into the anus is known and not penetrating, is by inserting the tip of your finger into the anus, and gently inserting a thread of sinew or iron in the fistula when there is no tortuosity."
"But if there is tortuosity in that one, then insert a thin thread of lead or horsehair into it until you feel the thread or the hair on your finger."
"And if you do not feel that one at all, and there is no cause of discharge or worms or windiness through the track, as we have said, then know that it is not penetrating, and then you can proceed to the cure."
"And when the fistula is penetrating into the bladder or into the urethra, then its meaning is the emission of urine from it and prohibition of it until that place in medicine is consolidated."
"But if it is penetrating into the junction of the vagina or into the bone and there is pain in the area, then its sign is that the thread should pass through here, if there is not tortuosity into the bone, and there is pain in the area of the part; and that pus always comes from it; and that medication does not help, nor is it consolidated with an ointment."
"And in all those penetrating fistulas there is no complete cure, and the cure of them is the effort and futility of foolish physicians on which we place our trust."
"But in that one which is not penetrating and is not old, cure with iron is expected according to what I will recommend to you, and what I have already said."
"And it is that the pain wanders between your buttocks and mainly around your anus, raising its mounds inside, the cheeks of your buttocks leaning towards its belly, and gently insert a thread of lead or sinew if there is tortuosity in the fistula until you know where the thread goes."
"And if that one feels the pain around the anus, then it is necessary for you to insert the tip of your finger into the anus."
"And if you feel the thread already passing through the finger that you inserted into it openly penetrating, other than what you feel between your finger and that one or flesh, then know certainly that that one is penetrating; and therefore do not work on that one, for there is no cure in it, as we have said."
"But however some say that it is cured in some men."
"And of the medication by which one hopes for its improvement is that you ignite a cautery with fire according to the width of the fistula, as it is said before, and insert that burning into the fistula until it reaches around the anus; and again repeat it two or three times until you know that all those tissues surrounding the fistula are already burnt, which resemble the feathers of birds."
"And then treat it with hot poultices wrapped in linen until all those tissues that are burnt are covered, and also treat it with medicines that generate flesh and consolidate it, and if it is healed, well; and if not, then know that it will not be healed at any time by another cure."
"And if the thread goes in and does not penetrate into your finger which is in the anus, and between that one and the thread that is wrapped in flesh or skin, and sometimes the fistula runs along the surface of the thigh, then cut off the thigh from the beginning of the fistula, and you will see it cut with the thread, and let the section reach to where the end of the thread goes, and through the thread it will be released and healed."
"And then cleanse those tissues surrounding the fistula which resemble the feathers of birds, and do not leave any cause for them to remain."
"But if bleeding happens sometimes during your operation when you are cutting those tissues, then the harm that is done is from pus and a light instrument should be cauterized with fire or with an acute medicine, for cautery with fire has two good habits: it is burning of those burnt tissues, and abstraction of blood and drying out of humidity."
"And then treat it with hot poultices wrapped in linen or in torn cloth until the place gets warm, and then treat the wound with ointments that generate hard flesh and consolidate."
"And so medicines in which there is astringency and dryness, when the wound is healed then it is already healed and does not need repetition."
"But if the fistula goes inside the anus of the buttocks and is elongated from its surface on the body, then insert your finger into the anus and examine it with that."
"And therefore if the thread is cut and between you and it there is wrapping of skin or flesh, and it is close to penetration, then it is not an operation on that one but according to the way of faith and hope."
"And that cause can be managed in one of three ways: either cauterize it as we have said; or cut it off until the concavity of it is achieved through which you can enter your finger and perform the operation suggested; and do not proceed with cutting so that you do not wound the lachrymal sac containing the coccyx, and that accidents happen over the judgment of the estate without its will; and then treat it with water as we have said for strong wine will heal quickly; or extend that wrapping and cleanse that pus which dries out that until near to the anus as we have said, either with a thread or with another instrument of sharp point, and then cleanse those tissues surrounding the fistula which are in the section through which you can cauterize them; and then make an effort to restore all the wound by cutting it off, and if the opening above is not consolidated, and the fistula remains open in the parting of the buttocks, then pus will leak out because of illness." "Some fistulas are finished in this manner: when you insert the probe into the fistula, on the side of the buttocks near the surface of the body and on the edge of the anus, then take a probe with a perforated end, similar to those used for preparing hearts."
"Then insert the probe into that field enveloping it with five fingers or around those; and then insert the probe with forceps inside the fistula until you reach its concavity."
"But if you are penetrating near the edge of the anus from behind, then remove the probe from that path in such a way that you insert your little finger into the anus; and then pull out the end of the probe and adjust both ends evenly. Then tighten each one and leave it like that for one or two days. And when more tissue has been cut into the flesh, carefully remove that which is between those pieces of flesh which are between the two ends of the probe."
"And then cure the wound until it has consolidated and healed."
"But if the opening of the fistula does not penetrate, then make it penetrate in whatever manner you have prepared, but do not be too eager about it because otherwise you might injure the skin. And then heal that wound."
"The shape of the spatula used to split open the fistula is like this: one end is very sharp and the other end is not sharp, so as not to cause unnecessary injury, as sometimes happens."
"For the stitching of hemorrhoids from which blood flows through the incision."
"Hemorrhoids come in two kinds: either they are between the buttocks resembling small coal piles, or they are like hard lumps of resin." "And those that are small and large, from which blood constantly flows in one place, many of them, and some are outside the anus, and at its extremes."
"But those that are outside the anus are according to the months of little humidity, from which citrine water or a little blood with continuous flow comes forth, and they are according to the color of the body."
"And the treatment for that which is inside the anus is to command the patient to sit and squeeze until the anus opens and the hemorrhoids appear." "Then you grasp them with a forceps or your nail and immediately cut them at their roots."
"But if the forceps cannot hold onto those because of their humidity and softness, then grasp them with rough cloth or cotton or a wool pad, squeeze them out with your fingers like that, and immediately cut them at their roots. Then sprinkle some powdered myrrh on the incision so that it may cauterize those wounds instead; or cauterize them as has been described in the chapter on cauterization." "And then treat them with another cure until they are healed."
"And if the anus does not obey evacuation, then wash it with water from the anus and let it be gently evacuated when the patient squeezes."
"But if the hemorrhoids are outside the anus, then their cause is slight. Take them with your nail or with forceps and cut them. Then treat them with water as mentioned earlier until they are healed."
"And when you have made the incision, it is necessary to stitch them closed in this way: take a thread and wrap it around a needle, then insert it into each of the wounds above. Then make the needle penetrate into the other side's root, and wrap both ends of the thread perpendicularly on the farther side from the needle. Then tightly tie the hemorrhoid with a knot, and cut off the excess thread and remove the needle."
"And do this to all of them, leaving one untreated so that the excess blood may flow from it."
"Then place a cloth soaked in rose oil or wax on the anus, and have the patient remain in bed for some time." "And leave it alone until it has dried. Then treat it with a poultice or another cure until it is healed."
"And when they are old and do not respond to medicine, then you must open them with a punctum spatula or your nail so that they become moist, and remove the scabs from above which prevent them from healing. Then treat them until they have healed."
"Then scrape out those fistulas with a sharp point so that much blood does not flow and they are not irritated. Then treat them until they have healed."
"Know that 'almesamir' is another name for hemorrhoids, and they are not always red but resemble the head of a nail in color. They occur throughout the body, especially around the buttocks and anus, where they cause pain during bowel movements."
"And therefore it is necessary to cut what is in the hemorrhoid's path, grasp it with forceps or fingers, and remove it from its root. Then treat it."
"And if you wish, cauterize them according to what has been described in its own chapter."
"But a 'verruca' is a small, rough, fistulous prominence on the surface of the body. Many times they appear in many children."
"And its treatment: stretch and cut it, or tie it with thread or hair until it dries up." "If you wish, cauterize it according to what has been said, with fire or an acute medicine."
"But 'formica' is a small, downy or fistulous prominence on the surface of the body, especially on the forehead. When it is touched, it feels like an ant bite, and they appear all over the body."
"To treat it: take a quill from an owl or vulture feather and make it strong. Place the quill on the 'formiga' so that its circle encompasses all sides of it. Then rotate your hand with the quill until you have incised what is around the 'formiga,' and press down on the skin's surface to remove the 'formiga' from its root."
"And if you wish, do this with a copper or iron needle according to this method:"
"Make the tip of the needle thin, blunt (i.e. not perforated), and wrapped with wax to ensure that it slides smoothly over the skin's surface when rotated."
"And if you wish, cauterize the 'formiga' according to what has been mentioned earlier in the chapter on cautery concerning 'athley.'"
"On the shape of instruments used for cautery."
"Sometimes cautery is performed with silver, brass, copper or iron melted and hammered. Sometimes instruments are made small or large according to the size of the patient, as those that are used for treating young children should be small; and those used on patients with round buttocks or dolorous ulcers should have small cauteries."
"The shape of a large and dull cautery:"
"The head of the needle above which the bag is tied should be wide in this manner, and it should differ from where the bag is tied as shown here:"
"The extremity of the pus that is within it, which has entered into the anus, should be made deaf (i.e., closed) with a gentle, subtle motion; and on one side of its entrance there should be two threads, and on the other side one thread, whose width should be according to the thickness of the rays of pus, making a smaller one for a smaller [amount of] pus."
"The bag in which the medications made from bladder or sheepskin are placed should have an opening of one palm's width."
"And it should be pierced by many threads, as it is turned; and the space between the threads should be the thickness of a finger."
"And then firmly insert into those threads a hot, warm cloth that has been moistened with ten parts of honey or wrapped around them; and secure it tightly with that cloth. And when the bag is placed in it, tightly close the opening of the chest between two fingers with strong pressure, and then wrap it around each thread: But note that the manner of wrapping should be such that you fill the bag with the medicine, which has been warmed according to the amount of tolerance of the patient; and make sure that it is not too hot nor too cold."
"And then have the patient lie on their back, elevate their buttocks and place underneath it something soft such as felt or wool; and then anoint the tip of the cautery with oil or egg albumen or fenugreek mucilage or similar substances; and then gently insert it into the anus, and then the assistant should take the bag and squeeze it two or three times vigorously until all that is in the chest has been evacuated into the bowels, and then remove the chest and have the patient bring their buttocks down to the bed."
"And if the medicine causes an evacuation of that kind, hold it as long as possible; and if he sleeps with it all night, it is even better for his recovery."
"But if you cauterize him in illnesses of retention of urine and discharge from the bladder, then you should repeat the cautery until he is healed."
"And if there are hemorrhoids or tender fistulas in the anus, then the cautery should be very subtle and gentle, using those cauteries with which children are cauterized."
"On the treatment of plagues."
"I have already spoken in the division of the treatment of plague about what was fitting for the book, and I say thus the treatment of those with my hand and medicines according to their completeness."
"The plague is various in accordance with what causes it and according to the location where the plague occurs."
"And the causes by which many times plague is brought about are thus: impact of stone, or incision with scissors or knife, or perforation with lance, or with club, or with arrow, or resembling those of many causes."
"But the plague that is in the parts of the body are thus: plague that falls on the head, or neck, or foot, or belly, or hip, and resembling those of the limbs."
"And I am recounting the treatment of some plague for which that reasoning and rule applies to other plague as well."
"And I will begin with simple head wounds, because the reminder of composite ones will come at the beginning of the third chapter."
"So I say that when a simple wound occurs in the head and it is not a fracture, then consider whether it was caused by an impact with stone or similar. If the chain has only been broken and the wound is large and you fear that apostema caut may happen afterwards, then quickly perform cephalic flebotomy and do not delay this; and remove from there as much blood according to the quantity of its virtue if no other cause prohibits flebotomy, especially if the blood issuing from the wound is little."
"And let flebotomy be done on the opposite side of the wounded part, and take care that the patient avoids exposure to wind and wine and coarse foods."
"But if you prohibit any cause due to smallness, then let the diet be reduced, and do not approach meat or wine."
"And if an apostema caut occurs over the wound, then cut it open and rinse with rose oil as usual or with wine in which there is styptic."
"But if you are sure of an apostema caut, then pause over the wound until it has its own blood and the air has not changed that powder which I will recommend later."
"And if the air has already changed that, then pause over the wound until it is healed."
"But if the wound is large or was caused by a cut from a sword or similar and the edges of it are not approximated by forceps, then approximate them with suture according to what I will recommend about the suture of those."
"But if the wound is already laid bare to bone and tendon and there is only a slight suspension, then cut that open and cure the wound with medicines and restore the flesh appropriately in place of the chain, and command the patient to avoid coarse foods: heads of cabbage and leeks and similar, until it is composed."
"And if you find putrefaction in the chain and it does not adhere to the bone, then cut away all that corruption and throw it out, and cure it."
"But if in these wounds there is an artery or vein from which blood flow can occur and it is not cut off by medicines, then inquire about the artery, and if you find that it has not been cut, then cut it with a scalpel or ligate it; and if necessity compels you such that what we have said does not help, then cauterize until the blood is cut off."
"And if these wounds are simple and small, then the cause of them is light. Therefore, you powder those with this powder, so that they may be consolidated before the air changes them."
"And the manner of the powder is this: take oil of unripe olives one part, dragon's blood one and a half parts, quicklime three parts; let all be thoroughly pounded and sifted, and let the wound be filled with it, and let it be held by good compression until it adheres to it, and let it be coagulated with its own blood."
"And then compress it above with forceps and leave it alone, and do not remove it while it is like that until it becomes apostematous, because the medicine does not depart from it until it is healed."
"And sometimes you can do this alone with cautery when unripe olives and dragon's blood are not at hand."
"And this same operation is done in large wounds when it is convenient to pause over them and compress them, and these are fresh wounds with their own blood which the air has not altered."
"And if the air has altered them, and especially when it is in summer time, then this powder does not have its intended effect. Rather, cure those with what we have said: pause over those wounds with clean dressings dipped in oil or with flour paste with water and honey until corruption stops; and then cure them with other remedies until they are healed."
"But if a fracture of the bone occurs in the wound and it is small, then extract that with a hook."
"And I speak about the treatment of fractures of the head in what follows."
"Concerning wounds of the neck."
"But if a wound occurs in the neck, then there is no difference in treatment between it and a simple wound of the head."
"But if the nerve of the neck is cut or an artery, then if it is a nerve there is nothing to be done but avoid treatment of it with anything that causes great astringency, such as verdigris and vitriol and similar substances because they harm nerves and harden it." "And do not compress the wound with any hot cause because the substance of nerves is hot and their continuation is with the brain, which is the seat of all members."
"And if it is cured with light medicines thus: the wound washed with rosewater, sometimes infused in sweet oil or not, and turpentine when washed with rosewater, and other ointments according to this manner, humid dressings."
"But if the wound is large, then perform suturing or compress the lips of it, and then cure it with powders until it is healed."
"But if there is depth to the wound or if it occurs in the lower part where putrefaction has taken hold, then perforate it at its deepest point."
"But if an artery has been cut in the wound and bleeding has occurred, then separate or dry it out, ligate it, or cauterize it if necessity compels you to do so."
"But if the vertebrae of the neck or all have been broken and the veins of the neck are saved, then approximate the lips of the wound with sutures over the spine of the neck and do not touch it; draw them together and reduce them to their natural figure, and then compress them with a suitable splint, and leave them alone for several days; and then cure them with dressings in which there is astringency and excitement until they are healed."
"But if the wound has reached the bone and caused fracture there, then explore it with probes, and then if there are fragments of bone, remove all those that you can; and what cannot be removed, leave it alone until the wound has putrefied and separated, and its inflammation has been alleviated."
"And if the wound is fresh then powder it with the powder that I have recommended for you." "But if there is a fistula in the wound, then cure it with that which is mentioned specifically in its chapter."
"If it is a puncture from a lance or scalpel, sometimes its depth should be considered. Then you should examine whether the boil has wind (air) inside it when the patient exhales; then you will know that the boil is deadly."
"If the boil is not deep and it's fresh with its own blood, then you should pause the operation at the first hour of powdering. Do not stretch that area so that the blood is not retained in its depth and does not return to the heart and worsen the condition, but pause there with gentle attraction, and wipe it twice a day."
"If the ointment is not available, then you should pause at the opening of the boil's mouth to wait for it to absorb whatever humidity there may be. And make sure the patient sleeps on the boil so that what is inside can drain out."
"But if three or more days have passed since the boil appeared and there has been no spasm nor heart tremors nor constriction of the throat in the patient, and they show other good dispositions, then you know that the boil is safe. Then cure it with warm compresses and any other treatment until it is healed."
"But if the boil's healing is delayed and all this time has passed, then you know that it has already become a fistula. Cure it according to its chapter."
"And if the boil is caused by a cut from a razor or knife and it's simple on the surface of the skin or back, then cure it with what is preceded by stitching if it's large, or with powder if it's small."
"But if there is already bone involvement and some pieces have been cut off from it, then twist the boil and try to extract those pieces if they are separate." "But if they are not separate, then leave them inside until the boil can be pushed out, because their extraction is eased that way."
"And for other accidental boils in other members, the treatment is the same as what has been said [for other kinds of boils]."
Of abdominal boils.
The disposition that occurs in the belly is either large, small, or moderate.
And small disruption is difficult to achieve in another way, and so reducing it is also difficult, unless you quickly try to introduce it back into its own place before it opens up and becomes enlarged, because then introduction into it is difficult.
And therefore the best disruption is moderate, because in that one there is no difficulty reducing the bowel, just as there is none in the two kinds mentioned above.
And know that suture of the belly is done in four ways, but two sutures are common and convenient for sutures of other boils on the body.
And the other two sutures are proper to other boils, but they are more proper in the suture of the belly.
And I will recount each one with exposition and explanation.
Therefore I say that when the boil is small and some cause of the bowel comes out through it, and it's difficult to reduce it, then this happens in one of two ways: either because of the smallness of the disruption as said above, or when swelling has come to the bowel due to the coldness of the air.
And therefore when this happens, then you should cut it open in such a way that you immerse a sponge or damp cloth in water boiled alone, or water with squinant, cyperus, and spica, and embroches, so that the swelling may be resolved within the bowel.
And sometimes it happens with this medicine in which there is astringency, and it's better that water alone be used for resolving the swelling.
And therefore when you see that the swelling has been resolved, then moisten the bowel with water in which there is altitude and mallows, because by this means entrance into it is made easier with little harm.
But if entering the bowel has been prevented by this treatment, then cut open the disruption a little with an instrument that has been inserted with smegma.
And the first treatment is better when it is appropriate and not necessary to cut open, so that there may be no occupation with cutting unless it is necessary and urgent.
Of instruments: what shape they should have
One end of it is cut off sharply and the other not-sharply, with a subtle point that is not too sharp like a spatula, but slightly obtuse.
And therefore when the boil has become enlarged and the bowel comes out, then its reduction should be done according to its natural form, in its own place if possible on that, because it's better.
But when the disruption is large and is in the lower part of the belly, then you should make the patient lie on their back, and elevate their buttocks as much as their head; but if it's in the upper part of the belly, then you should elevate the head and place the feet higher than the shoulders.
And likewise if the disruption is in one of the two parts of the belly, then always pay attention and consideration to this so that the part in which the boil is may be higher than the other.
And do this also for large boils and moderate ones.
And for small boils pause this: that you have prepared yourself, and especially make sure that the person who ministers has his hands between your armpits, holding the disruption completely with one hand and adjusting its lips, and especially uncovering it from that which should be sutured first.
And this is the common way of suturing: one in which you take a needle, or count needles according to the amount of the width of the boil; and then leave the end of the disruption from the middle finger of your left hand, and stretch the needle through one, so that you do not put thread into both ends of the cord with two threads on either side of the cord of the digits inside that part, until you have made it penetrate that part; and you already have four orders.
And then stitch with doubled thread around the needle, sometimes two parts at once, and especially join both lips and the boil by proper joining; and then leave the thickness of the finger and put another needle in that, and then tie it with thread like the first needle; and do not cease doing this if necessary until you have completed the contraction of the boil.
And let the needles be moderate between thickness and subtlety because thin needles scarcely incise the flesh; but thick ones have difficult entrance into the cord, therefore they should be moderate in thickness and subtlety.
And it is not necessary that the needle be fixed at both ends of the cord nearby because then the flesh will be scarcely incised and the boil will heal before its consolidation.
And do not prolong suturing so that the boil may not be prohibited from consolidation.
And then cut the ends of the needles so that they do not cause discomfort while sleeping; and you will apply powdered ointments on both sides of the sutures, which will hold the ends of the needles; and leave them until you know that the boil is consolidated.
"And this type of stitching with needles is most suitable for small wounds because it only takes one or two needles to close them."
"And the second type of stitching is as follows: you should administer it by suturing all four extremities (the neck and both ends of the scrotum) in one go, using a needle with thread that is fine and thin."
"And then, when the needle has pierced these four extremities, you should reduce the needle of that first part where you started, so that the thread pulls the skin together from the inside out, making the stitching like sewing cloth with which the skin is drawn tight."
"And pause between each stitch for a duration equal to the thickness of the little finger."
"And this stitch is known among men."
"And with this stitch, I sewed up the wound that had occurred in a man's belly who had been stabbed with a knife. The disruption of the wound was more than a palm wide and extended from the gut around two palms near the middle of the belly to the center of the member. And then I reduced it after 24 hours, as the gut had been forced out by the wound."
"And the wound was consolidated in the space of about fifteen days and he recovered and healed. And around that time, he lives for many years and returns to his former condition."
"And the other physicians had judged that he would not be healed. And by miracle it happened, for I did not heal him with any ointment, since there was no place where an ointment could be applied or any medicine used. Instead, I simply paused over the wound twice a day and washed it assiduously with water mixed with honey until it was healed."
"But you should know that there are two kinds of stitches proper to narration, according to the Word."
"And it is that you begin with a running stitch, and insert the needle from the outer part towards the inner part."
"And when the needle enters the bone and that muscle according to its rectitude and length of the entire body, leaving the extremity of the hip joint in which you inserted the needle; then make the needle penetrate from inside out at the other extremity of the thigh."
"And then when you have made that penetrate, now make it penetrate again into that same extremity of the thigh from outside to inside; and leave the extremity of the hip joint that is on this side, and make the needle penetrate into the other extremity from inside to outside."
"And then make your penetration with that through which you made it penetrate into the hip joint at the extremity of the thigh which is on the inside."
"And therefore start from this side and pull that with the extremity which is of the hip joint on the other side, and extract the needle from the bone which you penetrated, and then reduce it into that bone and sew the extremity of the hip joint which is on the other side with this extremity of the thigh; and extract that from the bone which is on its part."
"And do this once or twice and then do it again from inside according to that example."
"And the sum of this manner of suture is that you should sew with silk sutures with which you sew the skin, in such a way that you sew the hip joint once from the side of the bone's extremity, and leave that other time inside until it is completed."
"And the second species of suture which is particularly mentioned by Galen, and this is about it and for its treatment, is that you should sew it according to semilunar form with which some doctors sew it, in such a way that they approximate all parts to their corresponding parts according to nature; and they apply the extremity of one to the other extremity of the bone, and this is done as I have recommended."
"See that you leave the needle in the extremity of the thigh at your disposal from the outside, and make it penetrate into the inside in that sun, and leave two extremities of the hip joint; and then turn the needle around and make it penetrate from the outside to the inside in two extremities of the hip joint."
"And then turn those casings around, and make each casing penetrate from the inside to the outside in two extremities of the thigh on the other side than that which is on the contrary side."
"And this manner of suture is better than common light suture, and it is the suture of which a preceding remark was made."
"This is Galen's speech"
"And some say that abdominal suture is corrected with two needles, so that you insert into each a thread, and begin with needle insertion from where it is necessary to do so, and make it penetrate inside the other side according to the suture of those who sew the entrails evenly."
"And know that when rupture is in the middle of the abdomen, at that time abdominal suture is more difficult than that of other parts of the abdomen."
"However, the judgment of plague is judged by other plagues."
"The cause is this: when you manage to extract the recent plague with its blood before the air alters that, and return the intestine and cover it well and prepare it properly, then pause over that powdered medicine."
"And if the air has already altered the plague, then pause over those cloths which are present there and make them dry and wring out their juices, and let them be well washed and examined; and treat it thus as is the treatment of other plagues until it is healed."
"But if you are not present, then pause over that immediately because it begins to grow warm, thickens and changes color daily as I have taught you until it is healed, for you do not need another treatment in many situations when the plague is simple."
"But if you fear that the plague might communicate to cause injury to the principal limbs, then you should immerse lion's wool in good quality olive oil or rose oil and apply it around the affected area and leave it on."
"And if there is pain or putrefaction in its bowels, for this often happens, then mix it with wine and black treacle, and especially if the decay has reached the bowel and is difficult to expel from within the cavity."
"And know that that which is in the large intestine is of easier healing than that which is in the subtle intestines."
"And it is difficult to heal because the bowel called 'gegunu' does not receive healing for any plague that falls into it; and this is because of the great multitude of veins that are in it and its size which is in those, and because of the subtlety of its body, and because of its closeness to the nature of nerves."
"But if that which proceeds from the plague is flesh, and you obtain it fresh, then cut it according to your skill with which you reduce swollen intestines."
"But if it has passed into it some time and is now green or black, then you should press it with quicklime on the location that is discolored by it, so that flows of blood may come forth, for in the flesh are veins and arteries."
"And properly cut away that which is other than the limb, and hang two extreme points of the quicklime from the edge of the plague forceps, so that over you there may be alleviated the attraction of it, for then you should have discharge of the flesh and emission of the branch of the plague."
"Memorandum on Plagues when they occur in the bowel."
"When there is disruption in the bowel and it is small, then it is possible that it may be restored in some people, for example thus: one man who had been plagued in his belly with a lance wound and the plague was on the right side of the stomach, and the plague was old and had made a fistula, but it was handled gently and with ventilation."
"Then I pursued the cure of it although it was not yet confirmed in its healing, but I ceased to probe that which had been healed and the location was consolidated."
"And I put that I saw the location already consolidated, but the illness that befell him because of the mishap in his belly did not occur again; and no one was harmed by this mishap and they remained in their usual dispositions eating and drinking, and properly entered into baths and were exercised in their words."
"And already some experienced ones say that when plague occurs in the bowel and it is small, then it ought to be tied in this manner: namely, you should take frogs with large heads; and properly adjust the two lips of the plague and place one of those which has its mouth open over the two lips of the plague; therefore when it seizes on those and stretches its mouth, cut off its head, for it adheres and is not dissolved."
"And properly place another frog near the first one, and do not cease doing this with frogs one after another according to the quantity of all the plague."
"And properly reduce that and sew up the plague, and those attached heads remain in the bowel until the bowel is healed, and no harm befalls anyone."
"And it is possible that the bowel may be tied with subtle thread which is made from the gut of an attached beast, for it is more like a needle; namely you should take the extremity of these guts, and let it be well defleshed, and properly tie the extremity of it with a thread of it, wrapped around, and then insert that thread into needles and sew it up with that bowel, and reduce that in the disruption."
"And this manner of suturing with frogs is but a way of trust and hope."
"But if the plague is large and wide, especially if it is in one of the subtle bowels, for then it is only subtlety, and not healing of it at all."
"On the cure of zuchem (fistula)"
"You should know that every ulcer and abscess, once opened and ancient, becomes an ulcer, and is not consolidated and continually discharges pus without being cut off; then, in any limb it may be, generally it is called a fistula, which we call that same."
"A fistula in truth is a knotlike fleshy growth, hard and white, which causes no pain, having a cavity like that of the eye socket. Thus it is named that hollow ulcer or ulcer with an indentation."
"And sometimes in men there is a moist ulcer which discharges pus; but when the moisture is cut off, it heals in some hours." "Sometimes this moisture is thick and scanty, copious and thin."
"I have already explained all these causes, their signs and their treatments with medicines in the division."
"And so I want to tell you about the treatment of fistula, which is performed through an operation using a knife."
"And you should know that fistulas occur in all the members of the body; for some are related to large veins and arteries, or nerves, or the bladder, or the bowel, or the urinary bladder, or to one of the ribs, or to one of the vertebrae of the spine, or to one of the joints composed by composition such as that of the hand and foot. And some are close to the main member and similar ones."
"And therefore those fistulas which are of this kind have difficult healing and do not receive treatment, and dealing with them is a matter of trial and error and ignorance."
"And if there is one of these fistulas whose depth does not reach any of the places I have mentioned, and you hope and trust in its healing, and you want to know its extent, then take a probe of silk or iron, and if the fistula goes straight ahead, insert it into it."
"But if the fistula is tortuous, then investigate it with a probe of thin lead, because lead due to its weight follows the curvature of its course."
"And if the fistula has many horrifying branches, it is not possible for you to mark them with a probe."
"Then cleanse the openings for their openings, for the moisture used to cleanse that one will go towards the others and cause them to flow."

"And once you have stood on all those causes with true steadfastness, then proceed to the treatment according to your confidence: and it is that you consider now whether the fistula is apparent near or in a safe place, far from joint, nerve, artery, vein, or any of the places which yield to you and are spoken of."

"Of bone cutting and sawing."
"Extremities can be shortened either due to an intrinsic cause or an extrinsic cause. This may happen because you have treated the corruption with medicines and yet there is no improvement. Sometimes, the corruption may spread to other members without any apparent cause. In such cases, it is necessary that you incise that member where the corruption occurs so that the illness can be alleviated from death or malice, which is a greater damage to the member."
"And the sign of this is that the member becomes black where it has been burned, even though no fire was there. Or, putrefaction approaches with blackening within which corruption occurs and extends throughout the entire body; therefore, you should incise that one."
"And similarly, if corruption is due to the bite of some venomous cause such as that of a scorpion, mare's tail, viper, or similar ones."
"And if the corruption or bite is at the tip of the finger, then you should incise the finger and not allow the corruption to spread to the hand."
"And similarly, if it extends to the hand, then you should incise that one from the wrist joint so that corruption does not spread to the arm."
"And if it goes further than this, then you should incise the arm at the elbow joint."
"And if corruption passes beyond this and even reaches near the elbow joint, then it is the death of the illness. Administering another cause for cure at that point requires a larger amount of virtue."
"And similarly, if corruption extends to the toe of the foot, then you should incise that one at one of its joints."
"And if it reaches the heel, then you should amputate all of the foot." "But if it can reach the ankle, then you should incise the calf at the ankle joint."
"And if corruption has already reached the ankle, then there is nothing else to be done except to abandon it to death."

Then extend one ligament at each end and another on top. Separate the flesh between two ligaments using a broad spatula until all the flesh is exposed, then incise or saw it."

"The treatment of sinus problems and the quality of cleansing with medications."
"When an abscess occurs in certain flesh members and the space of the abscess is prolonged until it collects pus, and then it ruptures and perforates, and the pus comes out, leaving the place empty like a vessel, and the cord that remains above it is like a thin cloth, and there has been no further corruption, and it does not impress upon the bone or nerve or ligament, it is called a sinus, and it is not called a fistula."
"But if the space is prolonged until corruption impresses upon some member, then it is called a fistula and not a sinus."
"And the treatment of it is that you incise that cord completely as it revolves, and especially when it is thinned out and made like cloth, making sure that it does not adhere to the place due to its corruption."
"But if you hope that the cord will adhere and that that corruption has not yet reached its end, and there is an opening in the cord on the surface, then you treat it with a clyster."
"And if you consider the sinus, then if it is large and the arm that goes into it has a foul odor, then you cleans it with the Egyptian medicament which is made of oil, vinegar, and cinammon received in equal parts, put together in a vessel, and cooked over the fire until it reaches the consistency of honey."
"And then you take from it what is necessary and dissolve it with water and honey, and cleans the sinus with that, and strengthen the opening of it, leaving the medicine in it for a period of two hours."
"And then extract it with precision, and do this for so many days until the sinus is cleansed and the pus is removed."
"And sometimes it is cleaned with water of ashes when this medicament is not present. And if you take the ash of vine wood and put it on the water, then boil it and cleanse that with it until you are sure that the sinus has opened."
"And if the patient cannot tolerate the Egyptian medicament or the water of ashes, then cleanse it with water and honey mixed together in equal parts, and also use wine and honey mixed together, for the property of honey is to cleanse and wash, and wine causes the sinus to adhere, especially when there is an excess of astringency and dryness in the wine."
"And when you do this several times and are sure that the sinus has been removed, then cleanse it with something that causes flesh to grow in it."
"And if you take some refined diaphoretic ointment and dissolve it with rose oil and astingent wine, or use some other medicines and ointments that have the properties that I have already written about in the treatise on ointments."
"And if the opening of the sinus is narrow and the cannula of the clyster cannot be received into it, then widen it gradually with a small file, pausing in it with hot water wrapped in Egyptian or basilicon ointment until it has been widened."
"And similarly if the opening is wide, then bring together the lips of it with stitches and leave in it the quantity that intervenes between the clyster without addition."
"And if the opening of the sinus from which the arm emerges is raised up on its sides, then dry it with pus in a place that is low down so that the arm may run freely within it, for when the arm is compressed by the pressure of the sinus, flesh will be generated there."
"And if it is not possible for you to dry the sinus in the area of the pus as you wish, then prepare the member with preparation so that the arm runs freely through it according to what pleases you and without any cause of retention remaining in it."
"But remove that which is on the opening of the sinus at every hour so that what has adhered to it may be discharged from the arm." "And so that you may know whether what flows out of the arm is much or little, whether it is digested or undigested."
"And now you shall consider the place of that joint, whether in it the patient feels pain or not, and if it is inflamed."
"And when your medication is prolonged in this manner, and you see that the matter which is cast upon the opening of the joint has already adhered or nearly adheres, then on the third day, carefully detach it; but when you detach it, immediately change the bandage for another one and renew the ointment."
"But if from the joint a rather long space has yawned with subtle virus, then do not despair of its adhesion, for the healing of it is nearly accomplished; for there are some men in whom the generation of flesh in their bandages is tardy, and of those some in whom the contrary takes place."
"And if from the joint more than ten days has issued thick pus, then you know that the joint does not adhere; and if there is tardiness in the adhesion of the joint and this is the cause prolonged, then you shall adapt medicines for drying; but if the medicines are humid in their substance and in their virtue, they shall be made dry thus with fine ointment."
"And the last thing with which you shall cure it is to take some fine ointment and dissolve it in rose oil, and let there be placed upon it old wine vinegar in its substance; and thus apply that ointment with it, and use it."
"And it seems that in this action when there is no pus, fine ointment should be used with honey, when it is cooked until it is thickened, and use it; or else take myrrh and aloe and sesame, and grind all together and powder upon the honey while it is on the fire, and then strain that upon a cloth and apply it to the joint; and sprinkle that with the honey which you have cooked until it is thickened, and powder it upon the cloth."
"And sometimes it is administered with long pepper and the roots of celestial lilies (and that is celestial lily) and barley flour and centaurea, and use these simples or adjust them, grind them and sift them and powder upon the honey which has been prepared; and use it."
"And if the joint is prolonged and not healed by this treatment, then you know that there is corruption in its premise, and therefore make an examination of the bones or of the other hard members or of the ligaments; then you shall treat it with fistula cure, as has been said above."
"On the treatment of pimples, rubbed-on ointments, nail-cutting and adding a finger and cutting."
"A pimple is an abscess that arises from beneath the nail of the finger or toe of the hand or foot; it commonly occurs on other fingers and when prolonged its treatment is less valued; otherwise it is an apostema of cauterized apostema, or corrupted, and pus emerges from it which corrodes the root of the nail, often corrupting all of it entirely, and it sometimes extends its corruption to the bone so that there is a foul odor and the tip of the finger becomes reddened, and its color becomes dark."
"And therefore when you have done what we said in the division and your treatment does not relieve it, then it is necessary that you incise with iron all of the superfluity that remains of the nail, and immediately cauterize the wound with that, for cautery is greatly beneficial in this."
"But if the bone is sound and the nail is healthy, and yet the edges of the nail begin to cut into the flesh within, and it starts to prick and cause pain there, then you must make a subtle incision from the angle of the nail that pricks the flesh, and push it out and incise that flesh easily, and place upon what remains of the flesh medicines that corrode and consume everything; and then apply ointment until it is healed."
"But if corruption has already entered the bone, then you must incise and extract that bone, for it is never healed when the bone is corrupted."
"And if sometimes corrosion and corruption go into the finger, then you must incise that in one of its joints according to how it has spread, and then apply treatment until it is healed."
"But if the nail has received percussion or injury and there is intense pain in that place, then at first you must bleed the malady, and then dry the nail with a sharp spatula using a transverse cut from above to below, being careful that the cut does not extend into the flesh beneath the nail; otherwise you will cause intense pain and stimulate the birth of superfluous flesh in that place; then treat that place with something that alleviates pain."
"But what is said above, which is born in most men, is usually entirely fleshy, and often on the bones or often on the nail."
"And some are born at the root of the joint, or their birthplace is in some joints of the fingers." "But that which is born in one of the joints of the finger is not painful; and that which is born at the joint is often painful."
"And those that are born fleshy, the incision will be easy; and it is necessary that you incise it close to its root with a broad spatula."
"But that which is born at the root of the joint is difficult to treat; therefore beware of its excision."
"But in that which is born in the finger between the joints, it is necessary at first to incise the flesh of it with a round incision down to the bone, and then saw through it with one of those suitable saws fitted for that purpose, and then treat it until it is healed."
"But consolidation which occurs in the fingers between their many joints or through birth defects of man born thus, or from injury or burning by fire, or from contusion, then it is necessary to remove that consolidation until those digits return to their natural form."
"And then place between their wrappings of them hot oil-soaked wool so that they are not easily consolidated; and separate those or place between them a thin sheet of lead until it is consolidated as necessary."
"And similarly if consolidation occurs in some digits with the palm, then you must remove that consolidation according to how it is prepared and suitable for the shape of the limb."
"Of incisions of veins, there are many."
"Veins are many, and they are large veins wrapped around thickly full of blackish superfluity which come into prominence in the limbs of the body, and their most frequent occurrence is in the legs, especially in those of travelers, workers, and carriers."
"Therefore you must administer a purge to the body of black bile several times with strong expulsion, and then bleed the patient from the basilic vein."
"But the treatment of them with iron is according to two methods: one is that they should be incised and that black blood drawn out; the other method is that the vein should be raised up and all extracted."
"The section of it is according to this method: first, incise the thigh with cold water at its beginning until thick blood is resolved, which is the sediment of the thigh; then bind the thigh of the sick person to the superior part of the hip joint up to the lower part of the knee with a bandage; then cut through the vein in one place, or two, or three with an ample incision; then raise black blood with the index finger at the lower part of the thigh upward and downward until as much blood as you wish and deems sufficient has been removed."
"And then bind that [the bandage/wound], and instruct them to abstain from foods generating black bile."
"And perform the cure by phlebotomy when the veins are full, as is known to the patient."

"And then tie off the cord with forceps and remove the vein from all parts until it appears visible to sensation. And it is necessary for one who knows that wound to decline towards blackness."
"And afterwards, with evacuation having ceased, tie off that white which was like a cord."
"Then place that rope within so it may be elevated and cast off from the chain, and suspend it with a hook."
"Furthermore, cut open that section for three days, and then remove the chain from the part above the vein where it appears."
"Then elevate it and cut that section on the other side near the stalk; then extract it and elevate it so it may be passed through the second section; and then extract it from the section above."

"Form of the incident with which a vein is severed:"
